---

S01. Cover and Stage  

**Title**  
SARGE UNIVERSE  
The strategy game on Telegram  

**Subtitle**  
Deep, fair war inside your Telegram chats  

**One line summary**  
A mid-core strategy game that lives inside Telegram, built for instant battles, creator-run tournaments, and long-term war.  

**Stage label**  
Stage: Initial playable in testing. Raising to reach Series A-grade KPIs on Telegram.  

**Tagline bullets**  
- One tap from chat into a real battle, no app store friction  
- From group chat to live tournament bracket in under 60 seconds  
- Built for fair play, creator economies, and long-run elder game  

**Footer**  
Studio logo  
Contact: [Name], [Role], [Email], [Telegram handle]  



S02. Vision and Investment Highlights  

**Title**  
Vision and investment highlights  

**Vision**  
Sarge Universe is a deep, session-friendly war game that runs entirely inside Telegram. Players drop from chat links straight into battles, then grow persistent armies, bases, and alliances over time.  

At scale, Sarge becomes the reference strategy franchise on Telegram: fair by design, creator powered, and capable of supporting millions of daily players and tournaments across regions.  

**Why this is a compelling bet**  

Instant tournament creation  
- From group chat to live, competitive bracket in under 60 seconds.  
- Self-serve tools let creators host events and turn their communities into content engines.  

Viral replay mechanism  
- Every raid generates shareable content.  
- Replay links drive re-entry and new installs directly inside chats.  

Clear, fair monetisation model  
- Cosmetics and Battle Pass with transparent attach targets.  
- Price ladder from entry packs at £0.99 up to £49.99 prestige bundles, designed to monetise identity and status, not power.  

Experienced team and early community signal  
- Shipped strategy titles, scaled live ops, and built platform-grade backend and data pipelines.  
- 2,400 alpha waitlist sign-ups in the first 3 weeks (Jan 2024) with around 34 percent weekly engagement in the Discord community.  



S03. Player Problem and Fantasy  

**Title**  
Player problem and fantasy  

**The problem today**  
- Telegram is full of clickers, tap games, and meme titles, but almost no true mid-core strategy with depth, fairness, and long-tail progression.  
- Strategy players bounce between heavy mobile 4X and PC, with friction between their social graph and the games they actually play.  
- Creators on Telegram have large, engaged audiences but no deep, integrated strategy game they can truly own, run events in, and monetise.  

**The fantasy Sarge delivers**  
- “My army lives in my chats.” One tap from a link, I am in a real fight within seconds.  
- I play in tournaments run by community leaders I already follow, with visible ladders and real bragging rights.  
- Money buys expression and convenience, not raw power, so I can compete without paying and still feel respected.  

**Future proofing for live data**  
Space on the slide for 2 to 3 real quotes from early players or community once external cohorts have run.  



S04. Game Overview and Product Today  

**Title**  
Game overview and current product  

**Genre and platform**  
- Mid-core PvP and PvE war game built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with web as a controlled fallback.  

**Current status**  
- Initial playable build in testing.  
- Core systems are live: base building, raid execution, replay sharing, and tournament scaffolding.  
- Early testers are providing daily feedback on core mechanics, UI flow, and session pacing.  

**Systems already implemented**  
- Progression spine  
  - HQ tiers, resources, and upgrade paths up to elder-game tiers.  
  - Multiple unit families and counters already playable.  
- Battle and fairness  
  - Real-time raids and skirmishes with clear feedback and counter-play.  
  - Matchmaking driven by skill and recency, not spend. No purchasable stats, units, or timers.  
- Tournament framework  
  - Player-crafted tournament tools and templates for brackets, reward pools, and formats.  
  - One-tap join from chat to bracket participation in under 15 seconds.  

**Content runway before and after soft launch**  
- Early HQ tiers (levels 1 to 5), two core battle maps.  
- Seasonal event 1 and cosmetic set A ready to deploy.  
- Roadmap includes map variants, seasonal events, cosmetic sets B to D, and tournament formats tuned for elder game.  



S05. Core Loop, Five Seconds, and Progression  

**Title**  
Core loop and progression  

**The loop in five seconds**  
- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel.  
- Drop into a raid or battle in under five seconds.  
- Execute core tactical decisions: target selection, ability timing, and unit coordination.  
- See the result, earn resources, and unlock new upgrades.  

**Extended loop**  
Build → Battle → Loot → Upgrade → Repeat fuels  
Watch → Join → Play → Share → Enter tournament → Repeat.  

**Progression arc**  
- Early game  
  - Learn basic controls, complete the first missions, and unlock the first unit families.  
  - Short, satisfying sessions designed to fit natural Telegram usage patterns.  
- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices and army specialisation.  
  - Alliances, squads, and creator-led tournaments start to matter.  
- Elder game  
  - Territory and map control, alliance coordination, and long-running wars.  
  - High-stakes creator events and prestige cosmetics drive identity, not power.  

**Design goals**  
- Multiple viable strategies without a single dominant meta.  
- Battles that can be read in seconds but reward deep mastery.  
- Progression tuned for years of play, supported by regular events and content.  



S06. Market and Why Telegram Now  

**Title**  
Market and why Telegram  

**Platform tailwind**  
- Telegram has hundreds of millions of monthly active users, with Mini Apps that run inside chat threads.  
- Mini Apps remove app store friction and turn curiosity in a channel into real play in seconds.  
- Virality is native: forwards, channels, groups, and bots give us organic rails that traditional app stores do not.  

**The strategy gap**  
- Current Telegram hits skew toward tap-to-earn, clickers, and simple farming loops.  
- There is almost no deep, fair mid-core strategy offering persistent armies, alliances, and elder-game wars on Telegram.  
- Strategy players and creators who already live on Telegram have no flagship war game built for the platform.  

**Proof points that Telegram gaming can scale**  
- Recent Telegram-native games have scaled from concept to tens of millions of players in weeks when aligned with the platform’s rails.  
- Sarge applies that growth potential to a mid-core strategy experience rather than another clicker or farm.  

**What Sarge unlocks**  
- A flagship mid-core strategy franchise that runs natively inside Telegram.  
- A new class of creator-owned tournaments and events inside chat, not bolted on via external streams and tools.  



S07. Competition and Positioning  

**Title**  
Competition and positioning  

**Depth and skill**  
- Sarge Universe  
  - Full army building, tech choices, and elder game with multiple viable metas.  
- Telegram tap games  
  - Light progression and simple loops; often one obvious optimal path.  
- Classic mobile 4X or war games  
  - Deep but grind-heavy with chores, time gates, and high friction.  

**Friction and access**  
- Sarge Universe  
  - Opens from a link in chat straight into combat, no install step.  
- Telegram tap games  
  - Also instant, but built around thin mechanics.  
- Classic 4X or war  
  - App store page, download, install, long tutorial before the first meaningful fight.  

**Fairness and monetisation**  
- Sarge Universe  
  - Cosmetics-first economy, no pay for power.  
  - Clear published guardrails for monetisation to protect fairness and retention.  
- Telegram tap games  
  - Ad-heavy or tap-to-earn, with minimal design around fairness and elder game.  
- Classic 4X or war  
  - Reliant on purchasing power, time skips, and aggressive VIP ladders.  

**Social and creator upside**  
- Sarge Universe  
  - Built-in tools for creators to host tournaments, share replays, and earn revenue.  
- Telegram tap games  
  - Creators mostly drive traffic, not in-game events.  
- Classic 4X or war  
  - Creators operate outside the game via streams and videos, with limited in-game surface.  

**Positioning line**  
Sarge combines Telegram’s instant rails with deep, fair strategy and a creator economy that existing games on and off Telegram do not offer.  



S08. Traction, Signals, and 30-Day Validation Path  

**Title**  
Traction and validation plan  

**Current status**  
- Initial playable in testing on Telegram.  
- First external cohorts targeted for [Month Year] in priority regions.  
- Goal: reach the Base KPI gates defined in our model within the first 6 to 12 months of soft launch.  

**Early signals from community and prototype**  
- 2,400 alpha waitlist sign-ups in the first 3 weeks (Jan 2024).  
- Around 34 percent weekly engagement in the Discord community.  
- Internal testing build shows complete loop execution in 10 to 12 second gameplay captures.  

**Key forecast metrics to validate in first cohorts**  
- Retention Base forecast  
  - D1: 50 percent  
  - D7: 19 percent  
  - D30: 9 percent  
- Funnel and virality targets from the current model  
  - Tap to first session conversion: about 95 percent of deep-linked users.  
  - Share and re-entry: around 35 percent of players share at least one replay; around 22 percent of shared recipients start a session.  
- ARPDAU and CPI  
  - ARPDAU forecast around £0.55 by month 6 in Base case for scaled cohorts.  
  - CPI bands for Telegram Ads by tier:  
    - Tier 1: £0.50 to £1.00  
    - Tier 2: £0.10 to £0.50  
    - Tier 3: £0.05 to £0.10  

**How we validate**  
- Six critical hypotheses with explicit metrics, methods, windows, and owners as defined in the 30-day validation plan.  
- Every metric must hit its threshold before we scale spend or unlock the next tranche of cash.  

Small caption: all numbers on this slide are forecasts and targets from the current model, not live data yet.  



S09. Business Model and Fairness Policy  

**Title**  
Business model and fairness policy  

**Economy philosophy**  
- Cosmetics-first monetisation.  
- Progression power is earned by play, not by spend.  
- No pay for power: no purchasable stats, units, or timers.  

**Pillars and key KPIs by month 6 (model values)**  
- Payer rate: 2.2 percent blended.  
- ARPPU: around £20 across all spenders.  
- ARPDAU: around £0.55 by month 6 in Base case.  
- Battle Pass attach: 6 percent Basic (£4.99), 10 percent Premium (£9.99).  
- Cosmetics share: about 45 percent of total revenue.  

**Price ladder and SKU mix (first 180 days)**  
- Entry Pack (currency) at £0.99 with a target of roughly 8 percent of revenue.  
- Mid-tier currency and cosmetic bundles in the £4.99 to £19.99 range.  
- Prestige packs at £49.99 with a target of roughly 5 percent of revenue.  

**Fairness guardrails from the Sarge Universe economy policy**  
- Payer versus non-payer win rate gap under 1 percentage point at matched MMR.  
- Correlation of spend to win rate within MMR bands at or below r = 0.05.  
- Revenue mix at least 90 percent from non-power cosmetics.  
- Top 1 percent of spenders to account for at or below 35 percent of total revenue.  

**Retention and creator link**  
- Quests, limited-time events, and creator tournaments create reasons to return and to spend on identity and celebration, not power.  



S10. Unit Economics, LTV, and KPI Gates  

**Title**  
Unit economics and KPI gates  

**Forecast unit economics at Base case**  
- LTV by day 30: around £0.63 per player.  
- Target LTV to CPI ratio: 3.0x for 90-day cohorts in Tier 1 geos with mid-range CPI.  
- CPI scenarios (Telegram Ads, Base case forecast):  
  - Low: £0.10  
  - Mid: £0.20  
  - High: £0.50  

**Payback forecasts from current model**  
- Baseline payback: around 7 days for 30-day cohorts in optimal channels and creative formats.  
- Conservative payback: around 30 days for 90-day cohorts in higher CPI scenarios.  

**Building LTV in the model**  
- Retention curves  
  - Uses the Base D1, D7, D30 targets (50, 19, 9 percent) extended to D60 and D90.  
- Monetisation  
  - Payer rate and ARPPU from S09 feeding into ARPDAU and LTV curves.  
- Virality and re-entry  
  - K factor assumptions and replay-driven re-entry rates included in the cohort model.  

**Gate rules – scale only if**  
- Gate 1: Product market fit signal  
  - D7 retention at or above 19 percent in priority cohorts.  
- Gate 2: Monetisation health  
  - Battle Pass attach at or above 8 percent combined Basic and Premium.  
- Gate 3: Capital efficiency  
  - Payback at or below 30 days on key UA cohorts and LTV to CPI at or above 3.0x.  

**Safety valve and discipline**  
- UA and scale-up decisions are locked to these gates.  
- If any gate metric falls materially below threshold, spend is reduced, features and content are refocused, and additional runway is preserved.  



S11. UA, Growth Engine, and Go-to-Market  

**Title**  
UA and growth engine  

**Flywheel**  
Build and battle loops create replays and highlights.  
Replays fuel watch, join, and share actions in Telegram chats.  
Shares and creator events bring new players directly into tournaments and raids.  

**Channel strategy**  
- Organic and creator channels  
  - Replay links with one-tap sharing to Telegram chats via preview cards.  
  - Creator incentives and revenue share for top tournament hosts.  
  - Clans and persistent social groups to create daily engagement habits.  
- Paid channels  
  - Telegram Ads as the primary paid UA channel.  
  - Facebook or Instagram, TikTok, and YouTube pre-roll as secondary, tested only once LTV supports them.  

**CPI bands and creative cadence**  
- Telegram Ads CPI bands by tier  
  - Tier 1: £0.50 to £1.00  
  - Tier 2: £0.10 to £0.50  
  - Tier 3: £0.05 to £0.10  
- Weekly test cadence  
  - Three new creative variants per week, 72-hour evaluation window.  
  - Creative families: gameplay highlight, tournament invitation, raid replay, Battle Pass showcase.  

**Go-to-market phases and Gate 1 discipline**  
- Pre-launch weeks minus 8 to minus 5  
  - Trailer script and production, hero art batch, 300-player closed alpha.  
- Weeks minus 4 to minus 1  
  - Community build, press activation, whitelist microsite, Discord live, alpha tests.  
- Launch week  
  - Public release with creator-led tournaments, heavy replay sharing, and recruitment into squads and clans.  
- Weeks 1 to 4  
  - Onboarding, monetisation, and engagement experiments, all tracked by cohort.  
- Gate 1  
  - Scale UA only when D7 retention is at or above 19 percent in primary cohorts.

**Core leadership**  
- [Name], CEO and Game Director  
  - Shipped [relevant titles]; experience in F2P strategy and live ops.  
- [Name], Product and Design Lead

S13. Plan, Ask, and KPI-Gated Use of Funds  

**Title**  
Plan, ask, and KPI-gated spend  

**Raise**  
- Raising £10M to take Sarge from initial playable in testing to a KPI-driven Telegram live service ready for a full Series A.  

**Runway and gated roadmap (Base case)**  
- Around 12 months of planned roadmap with explicit gates and tranches, extending to roughly 24 months of runway in Base case scenarios.  

1. Months 1 to 2 – Alpha to soft launch  
- Themes: Core HQ tiers 1 to 3, first map variants.  
- Features: Base build, raid execution, replay sharing.  
- Gate: D1 retention at or above 45 percent, share rate at or above 30 percent.

2. Months 3 to 4 – Expansion  
- Themes: Seasonal event 1, cosmetic set A.  
- Features: Player-crafted tournament tools and challenge templates.

3. Months 5 to 6 – Scale Tier 1

- Features: Clan systems, moderation flows, replay hubs.  
- Gate: Payback at or below 90 days, LTV to CPI at or above 3.0x.  
- Tranche 3: £2.5M unlocked.  

4. Months 7 to 12 – Multi-geo  
- Themes: Seasonal events 2 to 3, cosmetics C and D, prestige content.  
- Features: Advanced matchmaking, creator analytics, localisation for around five languages.  
- Gate: D30 retention at or above 9 percent, ARPDAU at or above £0.55.  
- Tranche 4: £3.0M unlocked.  

**Rollback protocol**  
- If any gate metric falls more than 15 percent below its threshold, spend is reduced, features are reprioritised for retention and monetisation, and at least three months of runway are kept in reserve at all times.

Appendix A1. Risks and Mitigations  

**Title**  
Risks and mitigations  

Table: Risk, Trigger, Mitigation, Owner.  

Platform risk  
- Trigger  
  - Telegram changes Mini App, bot, or payment policies.  
- Mitigation  
  - Maintain direct contact with Telegram.  
  - Keep a web client and PC build as controlled fallbacks.  
  - Monitor policy and legal updates and plan for compliance.  
- Owner  
  - CEO.  

UA and CPI risk  
- Trigger  
  - CPIs for Telegram Ads or creator channels sit above modelled bands for an extended period.  
- Mitigation  
  - Shift mix toward stronger organic replays and creator tournaments.  
  - Iterate creatives weekly, adjust targeting and geo mix.  
  - Explore additional channels once economics support them.  
- Owner  
  - Growth lead.  

Monetisation and fairness risk  
- Trigger  
  - Retention hits targets but ARPDAU and payer rate lag, or pressure to add pay for power appears.  
- Mitigation  
  - Expand cosmetics, events, and status-driven items without touching power.  
  - Use surveys and telemetry to tune offers and bundles.  
- Owner  
  - Product lead.  

Live ops and content cadence risk  
- Trigger  
  - Elder-game engagement drops; alliances and tournaments lose momentum.  
- Mitigation  
  - Tooling and templates to accelerate event creation.  
  - Clear live ops calendar with backup events pre-scoped.  
- Owner  
  - Live ops producer.  



Appendix A2. 30-Day Validation Plan  

**Title**  
30 day validation plan  

**Objectives**  
- Convert forecasts into observed metrics on dated tests.  
- Validate that core loop and early game can hit Base D1, D7, D30 targets.  
- Validate CPI bands and early cohort quality for Telegram Ads and creator UA.  
- Collect first monetisation signals without overfitting to early whales.  

Table: Hypothesis, Metric, Method, Window, Owner.  

Retention  
- Hypothesis  
  - Onboarding and first missions can reach 50, 19, and 9 percent for D1, D7, and D30.  
- Metrics  
  - D1, D3, D7, D30 retention; tutorial completion; first win rate; time to first meaningful match.

  - A and B variants of onboarding and mission structure across cohorts A, B, and C.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 1 to 4.  
- Owner  
  - Product and design.  

Monetisation  
- Hypothesis  
  - A light cosmetic store plus an early Battle Pass preview can reach modelled ARPDAU and payer rate without harming fairness perception.  
- Metrics  
  - ARPDAU, payer rate, ARPPU, Battle Pass attach, fairness NPS or survey scores.  
- Method  
  - Limited-time cosmetic and Battle Pass tests with surveys and cohort analysis.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 2 to 4.  
- Owner  
  - Product and data.  

UA and CPI  
- Hypothesis  
  - Telegram Ads and creator campaigns can reach CPI bands assumed in the Base model.  
- Metrics  
  - CPI by geo and channel; click-through rate; install-to-battle conversion; replay share and re-entry rates.  
- Method  
  - Small, capped UA experiments using three creative families (replay, tournament, Battle Pass).  
- Window  
  - Weeks 2 to 4.  
- Owner  
  - Growth and UA.  

Success bars  
- If bars are hit  
  - Expand cohorts, broaden creative testing, and move toward Gate 2.  
- If bars are missed  
  - Prioritise product and funnel improvements, then re-test before scaling UA or unlocking next tranches.

I dont know if I believe you, as a team of expert investors and veteran mobile game studio leadership critic the flow and red team it

[ASSISTANT]
Assumptions  
- We are critiquing the *text deck* you just got from me (14 core slides plus appendices), not the older 26–slide PPT.  
- Stage is pre-launch, raising a “Series A style” round that is actually pre-data.  
- Your internal guide is the reference for structure and seriousness.

Plan  
1. Assess flow and structure as if reviewing the deck in order.  
2. Red team the content and assumptions as a skeptical investor and studio leadership group.  
3. End with specific, high-impact change list so you can iterate.

I will not sugar coat this.

  

## 1. Flow and structure critique

### 1.1 Overall arc

Current arc:

- S01–S05: Story and product  
- S06–S07: Market and competition  
- S08–S10: Traction, model, economics  
- S11: UA and GTM  
- S12–S13: Team and plan  
- S14 + appendices: Close and detail

Structurally this is fine and close to your guide. Problems:

1. It behaves like a **data-driven Series A deck**, but you have **zero live KPIs**.  
   - S08–S10 read like “here is how the game performed” when they are actually “here is what we hope it will do.”  
   - Investors will feel you are trying to wear a Series A coat with pre-Seed clothes underneath.

2. There is **no strong single hook** early.  
   - You do not lock in one killer thing by slide 3 that is uniquely Sarge.  
   - Instead it reads as “good mid-core Telegram strategy with fairness,” which is nice, but not arresting.

3. Text density is too high for decision makers.  
   - Multiple slides (S03, S04, S05, S06, S08, S10) are long bullet pages.  
   - For partners and GPs who flick, attention will decay before they reach your economics, which is where they care most.

Verdict on flow: structurally correct, but it feels heavy, over-explained, and under-proved for the narrative you want.

  

### 1.2 Early slides (S01–S05)

Strengths

- Clear that it is a Telegram-native strategy game.  
- Fairness and creator tournaments appear early and often.  
- The five-second loop is front and centre.

Weaknesses

- S01 and S02 repeat the same ideas: “mid-core on Telegram, fair, creator, millions of players.” S02 adds almost nothing new.  
- S03 and S04 blur problem, fantasy, and product. They are each stronger, but together feel like one slide split into two.  
- S05 has good content, but mixes loop description with design philosophy, so investors will skim.

Flow problem: the first five slides could be three if you were ruthless. Investors will feel they are reading a treatment, not a pitch, before they reach anything about money.

  

### 1.3 Market and competition (S06–S07)

Strengths

- Correct placement after product, before economics.  
- Telegraphs the platform tailwind and the strategy gap on Telegram.  
- Competition grid is clear.

Weaknesses

- Market slide never nails **one** hard size-of-prize sentence that feels credible and defensible. You gesture at numbers but do not plant a flag.  
- Competition slide is qualitative only. No hint of performance ranges or specific titles.  
- You do not crystallise why Sarge has **any durable moat** if a big studio decides to build a Telegram strategy game.

Flow problem: by S07 an investor still cannot tell “how big is this if it works” and “what stops Tencent or Supercell from doing the same.” That is what this cluster should answer.

  

### 1.4 Data, model, economics (S08–S10)

This is where a Series A investor’s brain turns on. Right now this cluster is the weakest.

Strengths

- You have a validation plan and KPI gates.  
- You are honest in a caption that numbers are forecasts.  
- You talk in the right language: D1, D7, D30, ARPDAU, LTV to CPI, payback.

Weaknesses

1. **Tone mismatch:**  
   - These slides *read* like “these are our results,” not “these are our betting lines.”  
   - Sprinkling “forecast” in a caption does not fix the overall impression.

2. **Number stacking without evidence:**  
   - A partner will ask: “Where do 50 / 19 / 9 percent come from? Why not 40 / 15 / 7?”  
   - ARPDAU around £0.55 by month 6, payer rate 2.2 percent, ARPPU £20, Battle Pass attach 16 percent combined, and LTV to CPI 3x inside 90 days all stacked in one place scream “we built a nice model,” not “we built a game and tested it.”  
   - Putting all of them in the deck invites a math fight.

3. **Flow within the cluster is off:**  
   - S08 mixes “status, community, targets, funnel, virality” on one slide. It tries to be both a traction slide and a model slide. It should be one or the other.  
   - S09 is half economy narrative, half KPI dump. It could be split into “Economy philosophy” and “Monetisation model snapshot.”  
   - S10 repeats some numbers from S08 and S09 in slightly different framing. An investor will check for inconsistencies and you will get tied up answering “why this slide says X and the other says Y.”

Flow problem: the investor wants “One slide: here is what we are betting we can hit. One slide: here is our unit economics and gate discipline.” You give them **three** slides full of overlapping forecasts, which is exactly where suspicion goes up.

  

### 1.5 UA, team, and plan (S11–S13)

Strengths

- UA slide understands Telegram reality: creators, replays, Ads.  
- Team slide explains roles and operating rhythm instead of just faces.  
- Plan and ask slide introduces gated tranches, which is sophisticated.

Weaknesses

- UA slide does not clearly separate **what is proven** (No data, really) from **what is hypothesised**. That is the same problem as the KPI cluster.  
- Team slide is generic without specifics of who did what before. As investors, we cannot tell if anyone has actually shipped a sticky strategy game.  
- Tranche plan in S13 is heavy with numbers and gates that echo S08–S10. It will feel like “too much mechanics, not enough proof.” Also, explicit tranching by gate is something many investors hate unless they proposed it.

Flow problem: you give sophistication and structure, but because there is no live data, it will read as clever theory, not earned discipline.

  

### 1.6 Close and appendices (S14, A1–A4)

Strengths

- S14 clearly states “why now, what this pays for, what is in the data room.”  
- Risk and validation appendices are the right kind of content for later reading.  
- Hiring and financial snapshots exist, so diligence has something to bite into.

Weaknesses

- S14 does not restate **the single sharpest reason to believe**; it just restates a bundle of reasons.  
- Risks appendix is thin on Telegram-specific or regulatory risks. It reads like a generic live service risk list.  
- Financial snapshot is still hand-wavy on ranges and does not explicitly tie back to the exact numbers in S08–S10. Any mismatch is a credibility hit.

Flow problem: the close does not feel like “this is the one slide we want you to remember,” it feels like another summary.

  

## 2. Red team: what a skeptical investor or studio lead will say

Here I will be deliberately harsh.

1. **“You are dressing a Seed round in Series A clothes.”**  
   - No live metrics, no real user data, but a full Series A skeleton with LTV to CPI, tranches, and gates.  
   - Makes me think you care more about models than about shipping and learning.

2. **“Your numbers look hand-picked to be comforting, not derived.”**  
   - 50 / 19 / 9 retention, ARPDAU around £0.55, LTV to CPI 3x, payback under 30 days, CPI bands that conveniently allow that, whales capped at 35 percent of revenue, payer rate 2.2 percent, attach 16 percent.  
   - Every number looks like textbook “good F2P,” not something messy and real.

3. **“If fairness is this strict, where is the proof you can monetise?”**  
   - You proudly state no pay for power, extremely narrow payer/non-payer win rate gap, low correlation between spend and win rate.  
   - That is noble. On a risk basis, I immediately ask: who has proven you can get to those ARPDAU and LTV numbers with **only** cosmetics and status in a hardcore war audience? Where is the comparative reference?

4. **“Where is your moat if Telegram gaming explodes?”**  
   - You explain the platform and the gap, but do not convince me that Sarge is three steps ahead of any copycat on design, tech, or distribution.  
   - I see no unique tech (beyond Telegram integration) and no IP hook.

5. **“You are over-fitting the spreadsheet.”**  
   - The deck spends more energy on thresholds, gates, tranches, and KPIs than on the feel and uniqueness of the game and community.  
   - I worry you will optimise your way to a good spreadsheet and a bland product.

6. **“Have you actually shipped and operated something like this before?”**  
   - Team slide is generic. There is no “this person led X at Y and grew it to Z.”  
   - As a studio lead, I cannot see the execution muscle.

7. **“The deck is hard work to read.”**  
   - Too many words per slide.  
   - Too many similar numbers repeated across slides.  
   - Not enough visuals, examples, or player-level stories.

This is not fatal, but for a panel that sees a lot of decks, these are the default objections.

  

## 3. Priority changes to move toward 10 of 10 for your stage

You asked specifically for “fix the damn deck,” so here is a high-impact change set. This is not rewriting, this is *surgery*.

### 3.1 Clarify stage and honesty in the *first* five slides

- In S01 or S02, have a single clear line:  
  “We are pre-launch on Telegram, using Series A-grade models and gates to manage a pre-Series A round.”  
- This explicitly defuses the “fake Series A” objection.  
- Make it explicit that S08–S10 are **target lanes**, not performance.

  

### 3.2 Collapse and sharpen the opening

- Merge S02 and S03 into a single slide:  
  “Vision and problem” with one short paragraph and three bullets.  
- Use S04 for “Game overview and five-second loop” only, not long lists of systems.  
- Move some of the systems detail into appendix or notes.

Goal: by slide 3 an investor can say, in their own words, “Telegram mid-core war, creator tournaments, no pay for power.”

  

### 3.3 Simplify the model cluster

Right now S08–S10 are a bowl of numbers. Instead:

- S08: “Where we are and what we are trying to prove in the next 12 months.”  
  - One block for current status and community, one block for **three** headline KPI targets, clearly labeled “targets.”  
- S09: “Economy and fairness policy.”  
  - Narrative only, plus 2 or 3 top monetisation targets (ARPDAU, payer rate, ARPPU).  
- S10: “Unit economics and gates.”  
  - One visual or one table that shows three CPI scenarios and resulting payback and LTV to CPI.  
  - A short list of gates tied to those numbers.

Cut the rest of the numerical clutter into the appendix where it belongs.

  

### 3.4 Reduce the number of different numerical claims

- Right now you mention: retention triplets, ARPDAU, payer rate, ARPPU, multiple attach rates, CPI bands, LTV, payback windows, K factor, share rate, re-entry rate, revenue mix, whale share.  
- For pre-launch, pick at most:  
  - Retention triplet,  
  - ARPDAU target,  
  - CPI band,  
  - Payback window,  
  - Whale share cap.  
- Everything else moves to appendix.

Fewer numbers, more clarity, less room for inconsistency.

  

### 3.5 Strengthen the moat story

You need at least one slide or one section that makes a serious investor think, “this is hard to copy.”

Examples:

- Unique tournament scripting and tools that let creators do things that look like esports, but inside Telegram.  
- Very specific replay sharing mechanic that makes Sarge replays more compelling than generic videos.  
- Deep balance and fairness systems that require long iteration, which you have already started.

At the moment, the deck reads as “first decent Telegram mid-core.” That is not enough moat.

  

### 3.6 Make the team slide concrete, not abstract

- Replace generic one-liners with explicit history like:  
  - “Ex-[studio], design lead on [title], grew it from X to Y MAU and Z in annual revenue.”  
  - “Ex-[company], ran UA budgets of £N per year across mid-core F2P portfolio.”  
- Show clearly that you have shipped, not just designed.  
- If you do not yet have that depth, this is itself a red flag you must decide how to handle.

  

### 3.7 Decide whether to keep or drop the tranche gating

- Many investors dislike hard tranche gating written into the deck, it smells like covenant.  
- You can keep the KPI gates as **internal discipline** and mention in conversation that you will use metrics to pace spend.  
- On slide, simplify to “runway, key milestones, and internal gates,” not “unlock tranche X of £Y at KPI threshold Z.”

This reduces friction on the ask and keeps discussion focused on upside, not conditions.

  

## 4. Short self-audit of this critique

- I have not re-opened the actual PPT or the Word guide here, I am critiquing the text deck and the numbers as stated. That means:  
  - If some numbers already differ between your model and the text, you must reconcile them separately.  
- I have assumed the model values are placeholders. If they are already tightly thought through, the concern shifts from “numbers are random” to “too many numbers in the main deck,” but the flow critique stays the same.  
- This is deliberately harsher than most investors would be in the room. Realistically, if they like you and the Telegram thesis, they will lean in. The goal here is to surface reasons they might not.

If you want to move toward a more believable 9 or 10 out of 10 for your actual stage, the fastest next step is to pick **one cluster** (for example S08–S10) and rebuild it with fewer numbers and clearer “this is target, not history” framing. Then we can move to story compression.

from pptx.enum.shapes import MSO_SHAPE_TYPE

def slide_text(slide):
    texts = []
    for shape in slide.shapes:
        if hasattr(shape, "text"):
            texts.append(shape.text.strip())
    return "\n---\n".join(t for t in texts if t)

for idx, sl in enumerate(slides, start=1):
    print(f"\n=== Slide {idx} ===")
    print(slide_text(sl)[:800])


[ASSISTANT]

    for shape in sl.shapes:
        if hasattr(shape, "text") and shape.text.strip():
            print("SHAPE:", repr(shape.text.strip()[:400]))

        title = sl.shapes.title.text
    print("TITLE:", repr(title.strip() if title else ""))
    body_texts = []
    for shape in sl.shapes:
        if hasattr(shape, "text") and shape is not sl.shapes.title:
            t = shape.text.strip()
            if t:
                body_texts.append(t)
    for t in body_texts:
        print("TEXT:", repr(t[:300]))

def show_slide(i):
    sl = slides[i-1]
    print(f"=== Slide {i} ===")
    title = sl.shapes.title.text if sl.shapes.title else ""
    print("TITLE:", title.strip())
    for shape in sl.shapes:
        if hasattr(shape, "text") and shape is not sl.shapes.title:
            t = shape.text.strip()
            if t:
                print("TEXT:", t.replace("\n", " | "))

for i in range(1, 16):
    show_slide(i)

for i in range(3, 11):
    show_slide(i)


[ASSISTANT]
def get_title_and_bullets(slide):
    texts = [shape.text.strip() for shape in slide.shapes if hasattr(shape, "text") and shape.text.strip()]
    if not texts:
        return "", []
    title = texts[0]
    bullets = texts[1:]
    return title, bullets

for i, sl in enumerate(slides, start=1):
    title, bullets = get_title_and_bullets(sl)
    print(f"\nSlide {i} title guess: {repr(title[:80])}")
    if bullets:
        print("  first bullets:", [b[:60] for b in bullets[:3]])


[ASSISTANT]
for start, end in [(1,14),(15,27)]:
    print(f"\n=== Slides {start} to {end} ===")
    for i in range(start, end+1):
        sl = slides[i-1]
        title, bullets = get_title_and_bullets(sl)
        print(f"Slide {i} title guess: {repr(title[:80])}")
        if bullets:
            print("  first bullets:", [b[:60].replace("\n"," ") for b in bullets[:2]])

## 2. Example: fully rewritten S08 slide using your actual deck content

To show I am no longer freelancing, here is one complete slide built directly from your material.

**S08. Traction and 30-day validation plan**  
(based on slides 4 and 19)

Title  
Traction and 30-day validation plan  

Body  

Status today  

- Initial playable build is live on Telegram with internal testers.  
- Core systems in testing: base building, raids, leagues, replays, and player-crafted tournaments.  
- Evidence available: 10–12 second gameplay captures showing the complete loop from chat into battle and back.  

What we are proving in the first 30 days of external cohorts  

- Convert forecasts into dated, observed metrics rather than spreadsheet assumptions.  
- Six critical hypotheses with explicit targets, methods, windows, and owners.  

Key targets and methods  

- Tap to first session  
  - Target: 95 percent conversion.  
  - Method: deep links from creator posts and referral shares tracked via UTM parameters in weeks 1–2.  
- D1, D7, D30 retention  
  - Targets: D1, D7, D30 thresholds as set in the unit economics model.  
  - Method: cohort tracking across variants of onboarding and early missions over weeks 1–4.  
- ARPDAU  
  - Target: £0.55 in the test window, consistent with the Base model.  
  - Method: weekend micro-tournaments with limited-time cosmetic rewards in week 3.  
- CPI by geo and channel  
  - Target: £0.10–£0.50 for Telegram Ads in early tests.  
  - Method: spark tests with three creative families (replay, tournament, Battle Pass) over weeks 2–4.  
- Share rate and re-entry  
  - Targets: 35 percent of players share at least one replay; 22 percent of recipients start a session.  
  - Method: replay link telemetry tracking share actions and subsequent session starts through weeks 1–4.  

Discipline  

- Every metric has an owner and a time window.  
- UA spend and roadmap decisions are gated on these outcomes before we scale beyond initial cohorts.  

All numbers above are **targets and forecasts** from the Unit Economics Snapshot and 12-Month Financial Plan, and will be replaced with live data once tests conclude.

This is almost a direct transformation of slide 19 plus the evidence line from slide 4, with explicit “target, not actual” framing to avoid bullshit.

S01. Cover and one line summary  

**Title**  
SARGE UNIVERSE  

**Subtitle**  
The strategy game on Telegram  

**One line summary**  
Mid-core PvP strategy game that lives inside Telegram chats, built for instant war and creator-run tournaments.  

**Round and stage**  
- Raising £10M to hit Series A KPI gates on Telegram  
- Stage: Initial playable in testing, pre-soft launch  

**Platform hook**  
- One-tap play inside chats, no app store friction  
- Players build bases, execute raids, share epic replays, and compete in player-crafted tournaments without leaving Telegram  

**Contact**  
- Steven Green, CEO  
- steven@thesargeuniverse.com  
- https://www.thesargeuniverse.com/  

Slide separator ---  

S02. Vision and investment highlights  

**Vision**  
Sarge Universe will be the first major mid-core strategy franchise built natively for Telegram, combining deep war-game systems with instant access, creator-run tournaments, and a fairness-first economy.  

**Investment highlights**  
- Instant tournament creation  
  - Convert group chats to live competitive tournaments in under 60 seconds  
  - Creator tools turn existing Telegram audiences into recurring events  

- Viral replay mechanism  
  - Every battle generates shareable replays  
  - Replay links spread through chats and channels, driving re-entry and new sessions  

- Robust retention and monetisation loop (model)  
  - Quest and event cadence designed to support high D1/D7/D30 retention and healthy ARPDAU  
  - Cosmetics and Battle Pass monetise identity and status rather than power  

- Transparent monetisation and fairness  
  - No purchasable stats, units, timers, or power  
  - Published fairness policy and guardrails  

- Seasoned leadership and execution  
  - Team and advisors with experience in mid-core F2P, large UA budgets, and platform-grade backend and analytics  

Slide separator ---  

S03. Player problem and fantasy  

**Player and creator problems**  
- Telegram users have seen clickers, tap-to-earn, and meme games, but almost no true mid-core strategy with depth and long-term progression  
- Strategy players bounce between PC and heavy mobile 4X titles, far from the social graphs where they actually chat and organise  
- Creators on Telegram have large audiences but no deep, integrated game where they can host events, tell stories, and share in the upside  

**Sarge fantasy**  
- “My army lives in my chats”  
  - One tap on a link and you are in a real war, not a slow tutorial  
- “My tournaments live in my community”  
  - Community leaders and creators run brackets, leagues, and weekend wars for their own audiences  
- “I can compete without paying to win”  
  - Spending buys expression, status, and convenience, not raw power  

**What players get**  
- Fast access: curiosity in chat to first raid in seconds  
- Persistent identity: base, army, alliance, and tournament history that live across chats and time  
- A social war story that unfolds in the same channels they already live in  

Slide separator ---  

S04. Game overview: genre, platform, status  

**What is Sarge Universe**  
- Mid-core PvP and PvE war game  
- Built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with a web client as a controlled fallback  

**Current status**  
- Initial playable build in testing on Telegram  
- Core loop working end to end:  
  - Players build bases, execute raids, and share replays  
  - Player-crafted tournament scaffolding implemented  

**Evidence of progress**  
- Prototype gameplay captures (about 10–12 seconds) show full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back  
- Internal testers using the build daily to tune pacing, clarity, and UX  

**Scope of current content**  
- Early HQ tiers and tech tree  
- Multiple unit families and counters  
- First map and mission set supporting raids and early elder-game experiments  

Slide separator ---  

S05. Core loop and progression  

**The loop in five seconds**  
- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel  
- Mini App opens inside Telegram  
- Drop into a raid or battle in seconds  
- Execute tactical choices, see results, earn resources  
- Upgrade base, tech, and units  
- Share replays back into chats or join a tournament  

**Extended loop**  
- Play loop  
  - Build → Battle → Loot → Upgrade → Scout next targets  
- Social loop  
  - Watch replay → Join squad or tournament → Play → Share → Recruit friends  

**Progression arc**  
- Early game  
  - Fast path to first raid completion in under about 90 seconds  
  - Unlock first unit families and basic abilities  
- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices, specialist units, and counter-play  
  - Alliances and creator events start to matter  
- Elder game  
  - Territory and league structures, alliance coordination, and seasonal campaigns  
  - High-stakes player-crafted tournaments with prestige rewards  

**Design goals**  
- Multiple viable metas instead of one dominant build  
- Battles readable in seconds but rewarding high skill  
- Progression designed for years of play, supported by structured live ops  

Slide separator ---  

S06. Market and why Telegram  

**Telegram as a platform**  
- Around 900M Telegram users  
- Mini Apps open directly in chats and remove install friction  
- Native social engine: chats, channels, groups, and bots already contain the social graph  

**Funnel advantage (from funnel slides)**  
- Mini App context: click-to-play in Telegram retains close to 100 percent of users, where download and install can lose up to half of all paid clicks  
- Traditional store funnel example  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → about 60 percent download  
  - Download → about 80 percent install  
  - Install → first play only after app open and tutorial  
- Telegram funnel example  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → play inside app, with near-zero drop between click and first session  

**Size of the wedge**  
- Telegram user base: about 900M  
- Telegram gamers: around 200M  
- Telegram PvP players: roughly 120M  
- Capturing a conservative 25 percent of PvP players over time implies around 30M players touched by Sarge  

**Virality proof points**  
- Native Telegram games have already scaled to tens and hundreds of millions of players (for example, Notcoin and Hamster Kombat)  
- Sarge applies similar rails to a deep mid-core strategy experience rather than another tap game  

Slide separator ---  

S07. Competitive landscape and differentiation  

**Where Sarge fits**  

- Telegram tap and clicker games  
  - Very simple loops, low depth  
  - Often tap-to-earn or meme driven  
  - Virality high, but retention and elder game shallow  

- Classic mobile 4X and war games  
  - Deep systems and elder game  
  - Heavy grind, aggressive pay-to-win, slow app store funnels  
  - Social experience often relies on external tools  

- Sarge Universe  
  - Deep strategy and elder game  
  - Lives inside Telegram with instant play, replay sharing, and tournaments in chats  
  - Fairness-first economy with no purchasable power  

**Competitive moat gains (from competitive moat slide)**  
- Tournament network effect  
  - Each creator who hosts tournaments brings their audience  
  - More creators → more events → more reasons for players to stay engaged  

- Replay library and education  
  - Every battle adds to a searchable replay library  
  - High level players effectively create free “how to play” content  

- Data flywheel  
  - Millions of battles feed matchmaking, balance patches, and content cadence  
  - Over time, this tuning becomes a moat that is hard for late entrants to match  

**Positioning line**  
Sarge is built to be the first deep mid-core war game on Telegram with creator-run tournaments and a fairness policy that supports both retention and monetisation.

    - ARPPU: about £20 blended across all spenders  
    - ARPDAU: about £0.55  
    - Battle Pass attach: 6 percent Basic (£4.99), 10 percent Premium (£9.99)  

**Price ladder and SKU mix (first 180 days)**  
- Entry pack at £0.99  
- Core currency and cosmetic bundles in the £4.99 to £19.99 range  
- Premium currency at £19.99  
- Prestige packs at £49.99 with around 5 percent of revenue mix  

**Fairness guardrails for soft launch**  
- Matchmaking uses MMR and recency only  
- Payer versus non-payer win-rate gap under 1 percentage point at matched MMR  
- Correlation of spend to win rate within MMR bands r ≤ 0.05  
- Revenue mix at least 90 percent from non-power cosmetics  
- Top 1 percent of spenders at or below 35 percent of total revenue

  - Iterate creatives and targeting  
  - Test secondary channels cautiously when economics allow  

Monetisation and fairness risk  
- Risk  
  - Retention strong but ARPDAU and payer rate below targets  
  - Pressure from players or stakeholders to add pay-for-power features  
- Mitigation  
  - Expand cosmetic, event, and status offerings  
  - Stick to published fairness guardrails  
  - Use surveys and telemetry to tune offers instead of adding power  

Live ops and content cadence risk  
- Risk  
  - Elder-game engagement drops; alliances and tournaments stall  
- Mitigation  
  - Live ops calendar, reusable event templates, and tooling  
  - Dedicated live ops owner

[USER]
do inverstors really give a shit about fairness first as a conept?

[ASSISTANT]
Short version:  
Most investors do **not** care about “fairness-first” as a moral concept. They care about it **only** if it clearly improves LTV, reduces risk, or unlocks UA and creator distribution. If it looks like ideology that might cap revenue, they’ll push back hard.

So it is not a selling point on its own. It is a **framing** for a retention / brand / risk story.

  

### 1. What investors actually care about here

For a Series-A-style games deal, the mental checklist is roughly:

- Can this get big enough to matter? (market, platform, genre)  
- Can it be sticky? (retention, elder game, social graph)  
- Can it monetise enough to justify UA at scale? (ARPDAU, payer rate, LTV:CPI, payback)  
- Can the team execute and not blow up the company? (track record, discipline)  

“Fairness-first” matters only where it touches those bullets:

- If fairness improves **retention and long-tail LTV**, that is good.  
- If fairness reduces **regulatory, platform, or PR blow-ups**, that is good.  
- If fairness makes **creators more willing to run tournaments and shill the game**, that is good.  

They do **not** fund you because “pay-to-win is bad.” They fund you because “this design gives us X-year earn, lower churn, and safer brand.”

  

### 2. Where “fairness-first” helps your pitch

If you frame it correctly, fairness can be a **plus**:

1. **Retention and ARPDAU durability**  
   - Less churn from non-payers who feel crushed by whales.  
   - Less meta-resetting powercreep, more confidence players can come back.  
   - That can make your LTV curve longer and smoother, which supports sane UA.

2. **Creator and community trust** (especially important on Telegram)  
   - Creators do not want to promote a game where their community screams “rigged, pay-to-win.”  
   - Fairness policy gives you a cleaner pitch to creators:  
     “You can safely build tournaments and content around this. We will not undermine you with broken power SKUs.”

3. **Reputational and regulatory risk**  
   - Less pressure around loot-box regulation, gambling analogies, and platform optics.  
   - For some funds (especially the more institutional ones), “low regulatory heat” is a real tick box.

4. **Differentiation vs existing Telegram hits**  
   - If most Telegram games are shallow, extractive clickers, “deep, fair, long-term war” is a distinctive *angle*.

These are all investor-relevant, but notice none of them require you to plant a big “FAIRNESS” flag as the main theme. It is a backing argument for **why your LTV is durable** and **why creators will stick with you**.

  

### 3. Where “fairness-first” backfires with investors

You are right to be wary. Red flags for an investor:

- It sounds like **ideology over business**  
  - “We will never do X, Y, Z” with no data, no trade-off analysis.  
  - They start thinking: “Are you leaving money on the table because you dislike the idea of monetisation?”

- It is not backed by examples  
  - No proof that your audience will happily spend on cosmetics and status in this specific genre.  
  - No benchmarks from similar games showing cosmetics-only can hit your ARPDAU/LTV targets.

- It is over-weighted in the deck  
  - If “fairness” is front-and-centre on multiple early slides, they may suspect you are compensating for weak monetisation or generic game design.

- It conflicts with your own model  
  - If you show very aggressive ARPDAU / LTV numbers **and** an extremely strict no-friction, no-pressure fairness story, they may think the model is fantasy.

  

### 4. How I would reposition it in the Sarge deck

Right now, we have “fairness-first” too prominent. I would:

1. **Stop selling fairness as a value statement.**  
   Treat it as a **design constraint that supports metrics**.

2. **Move the emphasis:**

   - On early slides (S01–S05):  
     - Lead with “Telegram-native mid-core, instant tournaments, creator rail advantage.”  
     - Mention fairness lightly, if at all.

   - On the business model slide (S09):  
     - Present fairness as:  
       “We make money through cosmetics, Battle Pass, and status items. Here is our model for payer rate, ARPPU, ARPDAU. Fairness constraints protect retention and trust.”  
     - One small fairness block, not half the slide.

   - On the risk slide:  
     - “We deliberately avoid pay-for-power to reduce regulatory and reputational risk and to increase creator willingness to partner.”  

3. **Tie fairness to hard outcomes:**

   Every time you mention fairness, immediately attach a business reason:

   - “This keeps non-spenders competitive, which supports D30 and long-tail LTV.”  
   - “This lets creators run tournaments without accusations of rigging, improving organic UA and event retention.”  
   - “This reduces the risk of being put under ‘gambling’ scrutiny, which protects UA and platform relationships.”

4. **Be blunt in conversation, not in slides**:

   - If asked in a meeting, the answer should be:  
     “We are fairness-first because, in our read, that is the best way to maximise *retention-driven LTV* for this audience on this platform. If data tells us we need more monetisation surfaces, we will add more cosmetics and status layers, not power. We are not here to make a moral argument, we are here to make a durable strategy game.”

  

### 5. Practical change for the deck

If you want, next step I would take is:

- Rewrite **one** slide, S09 Business Model, to:  
  - Lead with numbers and pillars.  
  - Shrink “Fairness policy” to 2–3 lines that explicitly reference retention, creator trust, and risk.  

So the answer to your question is:

- No, most investors do not “give a shit” about fairness as a moral banner.  
- They **do** care about what fairness does to retention, LTV, UA, and downside risk.  
- If we frame it that way, it helps. If we frame it as ideology, it hurts.

  - Over time, this tuning becomes a moat that is hard for late entrants to match  

**Positioning line**  
Sarge is built to be the first deep mid-core war game on Telegram with creator-run tournaments and a cosmetic economy tuned for long-term PvP play.  

---

S08. Traction and 30-day validation plan  

**Status today**  
- Initial playable build live for internal testing on Telegram  
- Core systems in testing: base building, raids, leagues, replays, and player-crafted tournaments  
- 10–12 second gameplay captures demonstrate complete loop from chat into combat and back  

**What the first 30 days of external cohorts must prove**  
- Convert model forecasts into observed, dated metrics  
- Validate that Sarge can reach the Base retention and monetisation targets in the model  
- Validate that Telegram Ads and creator channels can reach modelled CPI bands  

**Key targets from the validation plan**  
- Tap to first session  
  - Target: about 95 percent conversion from deep links in Telegram chats  
- Retention  
  - Base forecast thresholds: D1 50 percent, D7 19 percent, D30 9 percent  
- Monetisation  
  - ARPDAU target around £0.55 by month 6 in the Base case  
  - Payer rate and Battle Pass attach aligned with the business model slide  
- UA  
  - CPI bands for Telegram Ads between roughly £0.10 and £0.50 depending on territory  
- Virality  
  - Share rate target: around 35 percent of players share at least one replay  
  - Re-entry target: around 22 percent of recipients start a session  

**Discipline**  
- Six critical hypotheses with explicit metrics, method, window, and owner  
- UA scale and roadmap decisions gated on these outcomes before spend is increased  

(All metrics above are forecasts and targets from the unit economics model and 12-month financial plan, not live data yet.)  

---

S09. Business model and economy design  

**Economy approach**  
- Monetise cosmetic expression, status, and season participation  
- Power progression comes primarily from play and time in the game  

**Monetisation pillars**  
- Cosmetics and personalisation  
  - Skins, visual effects, banners, and UI themes  
  - Target around 45 percent of total revenue  
- Battle Pass  
  - Tiered pass with Basic and Premium tracks  
  - Model targets by month 6  
    - Payer rate: about 2.2 percent blended  
    - ARPPU: about £20 blended across all spenders  
    - ARPDAU: about £0.55  
    - Battle Pass attach: 6 percent Basic (£4.99), 10 percent Premium (£9.99)  

**Price ladder and SKU mix (first 180 days)**  
- Entry pack at £0.99  
- Core currency and cosmetic bundles in the £4.99 to £19.99 range  
- Premium currency at £19.99  
- Prestige packs at £49.99 with around 5 percent of revenue mix  

**Why this model**  
- Provides a broad base of cosmetic and seasonal spend without destabilising the competitive PvP environment  
- Keeps economic levers focused on identity, customisation, and event participation, which can scale with engagement  

---

S10. Unit economics snapshot and KPI gates  

**Unit economics snapshot (model)**  
- LTV Day 30 forecast: about £0.63 per player in Base case  
- CPI scenarios (Telegram Ads, global blended)  
  - Low CPI: £0.10  
  - Mid CPI: £0.20  
  - High CPI: £0.50  

**Payback forecasts**  
- At £0.10 CPI and £0.63 Day 30 LTV  
  - Payback around 3 days  
- At £0.20 CPI  
  - Payback around 8 days  
- At £0.50 CPI  
  - Payback around 23 days  

**Key Base assumptions**  
- Retention Base forecast  
  - D1: 50 percent  
  - D7: 19 percent  
  - D30: 9 percent  
- Monetisation Base forecast  
  - Payer rate: 2.2 percent blended  
  - ARPPU: about £25  
  - Battle Pass attach: 6 percent Basic, 10 percent Premium  

**Gate rules – scale only if**  
- Gate 1  
  - D7 retention at or above 19 percent in priority cohorts  
- Gate 2  
  - Battle Pass attach at or above 8 percent blended  
- Gate 3  
  - Payback at or below 30 days, with LTV to CPI ratio at or above 3x in 90-day cohorts  

(These are clearly labelled forecasts until validated by cohort data from soft launch.)  

---

S11. UA and go-to-market  

**Flywheel**  
- Battles create replays and highlight moments  
- Replays are shared into chats and channels as one-tap Mini App links  
- Shared replays bring new players directly into battles and tournaments  
- More players and creators create more events, which create more replays and so on  

**Channel mix**  
- Primary  
  - Telegram Ads with CPI bands from around £0.10 to £0.50  
- Organic and creator  
  - Replay sharing and squad recruitment in chats and channels  
  - Creator-run tournaments with revenue share and promotion support  
- Secondary (tested later)  
  - Classic mobile UA channels (Meta, Google, TikTok, YouTube) once LTV supports them  

**Creative strategy**  
- Creative families  
  - Gameplay highlight clips  
  - Tournament invitation formats  
  - Battle Pass showcase  
- Test cadence  
  - Three new creative variants per week  
  - Evaluate within 72-hour windows against CPI and retention targets  

**Go-to-market phases and Gate 1**  
- Pre-launch  
  - Trailer and hero art  
  - 300-player closed alpha  
- Soft launch  
  - Limited regions, Telegram-first campaigns, creator partnerships  
- Scale  
  - Expand UA and creator programmes only once Gate 1 (D7 ≥ 19 percent) and CPI bands are met

Appendix A1. Risks and mitigations  

**Key risks**  

Platform risk  
- Risk  
  - Telegram changes Mini App, bot, or payment policies  
- Mitigation  
  - Maintain close relationship with Telegram  
  - Keep web client as a controlled fallback  
  - Monitor policy and legal updates  

UA and CPI risk  
- Risk  
  - CPIs for Telegram Ads or creator campaigns sit above model bands for an extended period  
- Mitigation  
  - Shift mix toward stronger organic and replay-driven channels  
  - Iterate creatives and targeting  
  - Test secondary channels cautiously when economics allow  

Monetisation model risk  
- Risk  
  - Retention strong but ARPDAU and payer rate below targets  
- Mitigation  
  - Expand range and depth of cosmetic, event, and status-driven items  
  - Tune price ladder, bundles, and seasonal offers based on telemetry  

Live ops and content cadence risk  
- Risk  
  - Elder-game engagement drops; alliances and tournaments stall  
- Mitigation  
  - Live ops calendar, reusable event templates, and tooling  
  - Dedicated live ops owner  

---

- Full table from the Traction and 30-Day Validation Plan:  
  - Columns: Metric, Target, Method, Window, Owner  
  - Rows for Tap to First Session, D1/D7/D30 retention, ARPDAU, CPI, share rate, re-entry, and other core hypotheses

[ASSISTANT]
That “(about 10–12 seconds)” line is me pulling straight from your existing PPT wording about the gameplay capture length and dropping it into the text deck as “evidence of progress.”

Why I put it there originally:  
- Your PPT explicitly calls out a 10–12 second gameplay capture that shows the full loop from chat link to battle result.  
- I used that as a concrete proof point that the “five second into battle” and “snackable” claims are grounded in an actual build, not just talk.

Why it feels wrong in the slide text:  
- In the written deck it reads like a random timing detail instead of a meaningful KPI.  
- It is too specific for an overview slide and does not change the investor’s decision.  
- It also invites pointless questions like “Why 12 seconds and not 8” instead of talking about the game.

So I would fix S04 like this:

**Current line**  
> Prototype gameplay captures (about 10–12 seconds) show full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back  

**Better version**  
> Prototype gameplay captures show the full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back in a single short clip  

If you want to keep the timing somewhere for product nerds, we can stash it in an appendix or speaker notes instead of the main deck.

S01. Cover and one line summary  

**Title**  
SARGE UNIVERSE  

**Subtitle**  
The strategy game on Telegram  

**One line summary**  
Mid-core PvP strategy game that lives inside Telegram chats, built for instant war and creator-run tournaments.  

**Round and stage**  
- Raising £10M to hit Series A KPI gates on Telegram  
- Stage: Initial playable in testing, pre-soft launch  

**Platform hook**  
- One-tap play inside chats, no app store friction  
- Players build bases, execute raids, share replays, and compete in player-crafted tournaments without leaving Telegram  

**Contact**  
- Steven Green, CEO  
- steven@thesargeuniverse.com  
- https://www.thesargeuniverse.com/  

Slide break: ---  

S02. Vision and investment highlights  

**Vision**  
Sarge Universe aims to be the first major mid-core strategy franchise built natively for Telegram, combining deep war-game systems with instant access, creator-run tournaments, and a cosmetic-driven economy.  

**Investment highlights**  

- Instant tournament creation  
  - Convert group chats to live competitive tournaments in under 60 seconds  
  - Creator tools turn existing Telegram audiences into recurring events  

- Viral replay mechanism  
  - Every battle generates shareable replays  
  - Replay links spread through chats and channels, driving re-entry and new sessions  

- Retention and monetisation loop (model)  
  - Quest and event cadence designed to support strong D1/D7/D30 retention and healthy ARPDAU  
  - Cosmetics and Battle Pass monetise identity and participation in seasons and events  

- Clear monetisation design  
  - Defined price ladder and attach targets across cosmetics, passes, and bundles  

- Leadership and execution  
  - Team and advisors with experience in mid-core F2P, large UA budgets, and platform-grade backend and analytics  

Slide break: ---  

S03. Player problem and fantasy  

**Player and creator problems**  
- Telegram users have seen tap games and meme games, but almost no true mid-core strategy with depth and long-term progression  
- Strategy players bounce between PC and heavy mobile 4X titles, far from the chats where they actually organise  
- Creators on Telegram have large audiences but no deep, integrated game where they can host events, tell stories, and share upside  

**Sarge fantasy**  
- “My army lives in my chats”  
  - One tap on a link and you are in a real fight, not a slow tutorial  
- “My tournaments live in my community”  
  - Community leaders and creators run brackets, leagues, and weekend wars for their own audiences  

**What players get**  
- Fast access  
  - Curiosity in chat to first raid in seconds  
- Persistent identity  
  - Base, army, alliance, and tournament history that live across chats and time  
- A social war story  
  - Ongoing conflict that plays out in the same channels they already use every day  

Slide break: ---  

S04. Game overview – genre, platform, status  

**What is Sarge Universe**  
- Mid-core PvP and PvE war game  
- Built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with a web client as a controlled fallback  

**Current status**  
- Initial playable build in testing on Telegram  
- Core loop working end to end  
  - Players build bases, execute raids, and share replays  
  - Player-crafted tournament scaffolding implemented  

**Evidence of progress**  
- Gameplay captures show the full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back in a single short clip  
- Internal testers use the build daily to tune pacing, clarity, and UX  

**Scope of current content**  
- Early HQ tiers and tech tree  
- Multiple unit families and counters  
- First map and mission set supporting raids and early elder-game experiments  

Slide break: ---  

S05. Core loop and progression  

**The loop in five seconds**  
- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel  
- Mini App opens inside Telegram  
- Drop into a raid or battle in seconds  
- Execute tactical choices, see results, earn resources  
- Upgrade base, tech, and units  
- Share replays back into chats or join a tournament  

**Extended loop**  

- Play loop  
  - Build → Battle → Loot → Upgrade → Scout next targets  

- Social loop  
  - Watch replay → Join squad or tournament → Play → Share → Recruit friends  

**Progression arc**  

- Early game  
  - Fast path to first raid completion in under about 90 seconds  
  - Unlock first unit families and basic abilities  

- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices, specialist units, and counter-play  
  - Alliances and creator events start to matter  

- Elder game  
  - Territory and league structures, alliance coordination, and seasonal campaigns  
  - High-stakes player-crafted tournaments with prestige rewards  

**Design goals**  
- Multiple viable metas instead of one dominant build  
- Battles readable in seconds but rewarding high skill  
- Progression designed for years of play, supported by structured live ops  

Slide break: ---  

S06. Market and why Telegram  

**Telegram as a platform**  
- Around 900M Telegram users  
- Mini Apps open directly in chats and remove install friction  
- Native social engine through chats, channels, groups, and bots  

**Funnel advantage**  

- Traditional store funnel  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → about 60 percent download  
  - Download → about 80 percent install  
  - Install → first play only after app open and tutorial  

- Telegram funnel  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → play inside Telegram, with near-zero drop between click and first session  

**Size of the wedge**  
- Telegram user base: about 900M  
- Telegram gamers: around 200M  
- Telegram PvP players: roughly 120M  
- Capturing a conservative 25 percent of PvP players over time implies around 30M players touched by Sarge  

**Virality proof points**  
- Native Telegram games have already scaled to tens and hundreds of millions of players  
- Sarge applies the same rails to a deep mid-core strategy experience rather than another tap game  

Slide break: ---  

S07. Competitive landscape and differentiation  

**Where Sarge fits**  

- Telegram tap and clicker games  
  - Very simple loops, low depth  
  - Often tap-to-earn or meme driven  
  - Virality high, but retention and elder game shallow  

- Classic mobile 4X and war games  
  - Deep systems and elder game  
  - Heavy grind and slow store funnels  
  - Social experience often relies on external tools  

- Sarge Universe  
  - Deep strategy and elder game that runs inside Telegram  
  - Instant access from chats, replay sharing, and tournaments built around chat activity  
  - Cosmetic-driven monetisation tuned for a long-lived PvP audience  

**Competitive moat gains**  

- Tournament network effect  
  - Each creator who hosts tournaments brings their audience  
  - More creators → more events → more reasons for players to stay engaged  

- Replay library and education  
  - Every battle adds to a replay library  
  - High level players effectively create free “how to play” content  

- Data flywheel  
  - Battle data feeds matchmaking, balance patches, and content cadence  
  - Over time, this tuning becomes a moat that late entrants must catch up to  

**Positioning line**  
Sarge is designed to be the first deep mid-core war game on Telegram with creator-run tournaments and a cosmetic economy tuned for long-term PvP play.  

Slide break: ---
