You are right, that “Slide break:” label should not be there. Here is the cleaned deck with just `---` between slides.

S01. Cover and one line summary  

**Title**  
SARGE UNIVERSE  

**Subtitle**  
The strategy game on Telegram  

**One line summary**  
Mid-core PvP strategy game that lives inside Telegram chats, built for instant war and creator-run tournaments.  

**Round and stage**  
- Raising £10M to hit Series A KPI gates on Telegram  
- Stage: Initial playable in testing, pre-soft launch  

**Platform hook**  
- One-tap play inside chats, no app store friction  
- Players build bases, execute raids, share replays, and compete in player-crafted tournaments without leaving Telegram  

**Contact**  
- Steven Green, CEO  
- steven@thesargeuniverse.com  
- https://www.thesargeuniverse.com/  

`---`

S02. Vision and investment highlights  

**Vision**  
Sarge Universe aims to be the first major mid-core strategy franchise built natively for Telegram, combining deep war-game systems with instant access, creator-run tournaments, and a cosmetic-driven economy.  

**Investment highlights**  

- Instant tournament creation  
  - Convert group chats to live competitive tournaments in under 60 seconds  
  - Creator tools turn existing Telegram audiences into recurring events  

- Viral replay mechanism  
  - Every battle generates shareable replays  
  - Replay links spread through chats and channels, driving re-entry and new sessions  

- Retention and monetisation loop (model)  
  - Quest and event cadence designed to support strong D1/D7/D30 retention and healthy ARPDAU  
  - Cosmetics and Battle Pass monetise identity and participation in seasons and events  

- Clear monetisation design  
  - Defined price ladder and attach targets across cosmetics, passes, and bundles  

- Leadership and execution  
  - Team and advisors with experience in mid-core F2P, large UA budgets, and platform-grade backend and analytics  

`---`

S03. Player problem and fantasy  

**Player and creator problems**  
- Telegram users have seen tap games and meme games, but almost no true mid-core strategy with depth and long-term progression  
- Strategy players bounce between PC and heavy mobile 4X titles, far from the chats where they actually organise  
- Creators on Telegram have large audiences but no deep, integrated game where they can host events, tell stories, and share upside  

**Sarge fantasy**  
- “My army lives in my chats”  
  - One tap on a link and you are in a real fight, not a slow tutorial  
- “My tournaments live in my community”  
  - Community leaders and creators run brackets, leagues, and weekend wars for their own audiences  

**What players get**  
- Fast access  
  - Curiosity in chat to first raid in seconds  
- Persistent identity  
  - Base, army, alliance, and tournament history that live across chats and time  
- A social war story  
  - Ongoing conflict that plays out in the same channels they already use every day  

`---`

S04. Game overview: genre, platform, status  

**What is Sarge Universe**  
- Mid-core PvP and PvE war game  
- Built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with a web client as a controlled fallback  

**Current status**  
- Initial playable build in testing on Telegram  
- Core loop working end to end  
  - Players build bases, execute raids, and share replays  
  - Player-crafted tournament scaffolding implemented  

**Evidence of progress**  
- Gameplay captures show the full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back in a single short clip  
- Internal testers use the build daily to tune pacing, clarity, and UX  

**Scope of current content**  
- Early HQ tiers and tech tree  
- Multiple unit families and counters  
- First map and mission set supporting raids and early elder-game experiments  

`---`

S05. Core loop and progression  

**The loop in five seconds**  
- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel  
- Mini App opens inside Telegram  
- Drop into a raid or battle in seconds  
- Execute tactical choices, see results, earn resources  
- Upgrade base, tech, and units  
- Share replays back into chats or join a tournament  

**Extended loop**  

- Play loop  
  - Build → Battle → Loot → Upgrade → Scout next targets  

- Social loop  
  - Watch replay → Join squad or tournament → Play → Share → Recruit friends  

**Progression arc**  

- Early game  
  - Fast path to first raid completion in under about 90 seconds  
  - Unlock first unit families and basic abilities  

- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices, specialist units, and counter-play  
  - Alliances and creator events start to matter  

- Elder game  
  - Territory and league structures, alliance coordination, and seasonal campaigns  
  - High-stakes player-crafted tournaments with prestige rewards  

**Design goals**  
- Multiple viable metas instead of one dominant build  
- Battles readable in seconds but rewarding high skill  
- Progression designed for years of play, supported by structured live ops  

`---`

S06. Market and why Telegram  

**Telegram as a platform**  
- Around 900M Telegram users  
- Mini Apps open directly in chats and remove install friction  
- Native social engine through chats, channels, groups, and bots  

**Funnel advantage**  

- Traditional store funnel  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → about 60 percent download  
  - Download → about 80 percent install  
  - Install → first play only after app open and tutorial  

- Telegram funnel  
  - Impression → about 5 percent click  
  - Click → play inside Telegram, with near-zero drop between click and first session  

**Size of the wedge**  
- Telegram user base: about 900M  
- Telegram gamers: around 200M  
- Telegram PvP players: roughly 120M  
- Capturing a conservative 25 percent of PvP players over time implies around 30M players touched by Sarge  

**Virality proof points**  
- Native Telegram games have already scaled to tens and hundreds of millions of players  
- Sarge applies the same rails to a deep mid-core strategy experience rather than another tap game  

`---`

S07. Competitive landscape and differentiation  

**Where Sarge fits**  

- Telegram tap and clicker games  
  - Very simple loops, low depth  
  - Often tap-to-earn or meme driven  
  - Virality high, but retention and elder game shallow  

- Classic mobile 4X and war games  
  - Deep systems and elder game  
  - Heavy grind and slow store funnels  
  - Social experience often relies on external tools  

- Sarge Universe  
  - Deep strategy and elder game that runs inside Telegram  
  - Instant access from chats, replay sharing, and tournaments built around chat activity  
  - Cosmetic-driven monetisation tuned for a long-lived PvP audience  

**Competitive moat gains**  

- Tournament network effect  
  - Each creator who hosts tournaments brings their audience  
  - More creators → more events → more reasons for players to stay engaged  

- Replay library and education  
  - Every battle adds to a replay library  
  - High level players effectively create free “how to play” content  

- Data flywheel  
  - Battle data feeds matchmaking, balance patches, and content cadence  
  - Over time, this tuning becomes a moat that late entrants must catch up to  

**Positioning line**  
Sarge is designed to be the first deep mid-core war game on Telegram with creator-run tournaments and a cosmetic economy tuned for long-term PvP play.  

`---`

S08. Traction and 30 day validation plan  

**Status today**  
- Initial playable build live for internal testing on Telegram  
- Core systems in testing  
  - Base building  
  - Raids and leagues  
  - Replays and player-crafted tournaments  
- Gameplay captures demonstrate the complete loop from chat into combat and back  

**What the first 30 days of external cohorts must prove**  
- Convert model forecasts into observed, dated metrics  
- Validate that Sarge can reach the Base retention and monetisation targets in the model  
- Validate that Telegram Ads and creator channels can reach modelled CPI bands  

**Key targets from the validation plan**  

- Tap to first session  
  - Target about 95 percent conversion from deep links in Telegram chats  

- Retention  
  - Base forecast thresholds  
    - D1 50 percent  
    - D7 19 percent  
    - D30 9 percent  

- Monetisation  
  - ARPDAU target around £0.55 by month 6 in the Base case  
  - Payer rate and Battle Pass attach aligned with the business model slide  

- UA  
  - CPI bands for Telegram Ads between roughly £0.10 and £0.50 depending on territory  

- Virality  
  - Share rate target around 35 percent of players sharing at least one replay  
  - Re-entry target around 22 percent of recipients starting a session  

**Discipline**  
- Six critical hypotheses with explicit metrics, method, window, and owner  
- UA scale and roadmap decisions gated on these outcomes before spend is increased  

(All metrics above are forecasts and targets from the unit economics model and 12 month financial plan, not live data yet.)  

`---`

S09. Business model and economy design  

**Economy approach**  
- Monetise cosmetic expression, status, and season participation  
- Power progression comes primarily from play and time in the game  

**Monetisation pillars**  

- Cosmetics and personalisation  
  - Skins, visual effects, banners, and UI themes  
  - Target around 45 percent of total revenue  

- Battle Pass  
  - Tiered pass with Basic and Premium tracks  
  - Model targets by month 6  
    - Payer rate about 2.2 percent blended  
    - ARPPU about £20 blended across all spenders  
    - ARPDAU about £0.55  
    - Battle Pass attach 6 percent Basic (£4.99), 10 percent Premium (£9.99)  

**Price ladder and SKU mix in first 180 days**  
- Entry pack at £0.99  
- Core currency and cosmetic bundles in the £4.99 to £19.99 range  
- Premium currency at £19.99  
- Prestige packs at £49.99 with around 5 percent of revenue mix  

**Why this model**  
- Provides a broad base of cosmetic and seasonal spend  
- Keeps economic levers focused on identity, customisation, and event participation  

`---`

S10. Unit economics snapshot and KPI gates  

**Unit economics snapshot (model)**  
- LTV Day 30 forecast about £0.63 per player in Base case  

**CPI scenarios – Telegram Ads, global blended**  
- Low CPI: £0.10  
- Mid CPI: £0.20  
- High CPI: £0.50  

**Payback forecasts**  
- At £0.10 CPI and £0.63 Day 30 LTV  
  - Payback around 3 days  
- At £0.20 CPI  
  - Payback around 8 days  
- At £0.50 CPI  
  - Payback around 23 days  

**Key Base assumptions**  

- Retention Base forecast  
  - D1 50 percent  
  - D7 19 percent  
  - D30 9 percent  

- Monetisation Base forecast  
  - Payer rate 2.2 percent blended  
  - ARPPU about £25  
  - Battle Pass attach 6 percent Basic, 10 percent Premium  

**Gate rules – scale only if**  
- Gate 1  
  - D7 retention at or above 19 percent in priority cohorts  
- Gate 2  
  - Battle Pass attach at or above 8 percent blended  
- Gate 3  
  - Payback at or below 30 days, with LTV to CPI ratio at or above 3x in 90 day cohorts  

(These are forecasts until validated by cohort data from soft launch.)  

`---`

S11. UA and go to market  

**Flywheel**  
- Battles create replays and highlight moments  
- Replays are shared into chats and channels as one-tap Mini App links  
- Shared replays bring new players into battles and tournaments  
- More players and creators create more events, which create more replays  

**Channel mix**  

- Primary  
  - Telegram Ads with CPI bands from around £0.10 to £0.50  

- Organic and creator  
  - Replay sharing and squad recruitment in chats and channels  
  - Creator-run tournaments with revenue share and promotion support  

- Secondary, tested later  
  - Classic mobile UA channels such as Meta, Google, TikTok, YouTube once LTV supports them  

**Creative strategy**  
- Creative families  
  - Gameplay highlight clips  
  - Tournament invitation formats  
  - Battle Pass showcase  

- Test cadence  
  - Three new creative variants per week  
  - Evaluate within about 72 hours against CPI and retention targets  

**Go to market phases and Gate 1**  
- Pre launch  
  - Trailer and hero art  
  - 300 player closed alpha  

- Soft launch  
  - Limited regions, Telegram first campaigns, creator partnerships  

- Scale  
  - Expand UA and creator programmes only once Gate 1 (D7 at least 19 percent) and CPI bands are met

Appendix A1. Risks and mitigations  

**Platform risk**  
- Risk  
  - Telegram changes Mini App, bot, or payment policies  
- Mitigation  
  - Maintain close relationship with Telegram  
  - Keep web client as a controlled fallback  
  - Monitor policy and legal updates  

**UA and CPI risk**  
- Risk  
  - CPIs for Telegram Ads or creator campaigns sit above model bands for an extended period  
- Mitigation  
  - Shift mix toward stronger organic and replay driven channels  
  - Iterate creatives and targeting  
  - Test secondary channels cautiously when economics allow  

**Monetisation model risk**  
- Risk  
  - Retention strong but ARPDAU and payer rate below targets  
- Mitigation  
  - Expand range and depth of cosmetic, event, and status driven items  
  - Tune price ladder, bundles, and seasonal offers based on telemetry  

**Live ops and content cadence risk**  
- Risk  
  - Elder game engagement drops; alliances and tournaments stall  
- Mitigation  
  - Live ops calendar, reusable event templates, and tooling  
  - Dedicated live ops owner

Appendix A2. Traction and 30 day validation plan (detail)  

**Title**  
Traction and 30 day validation plan  

**Subtitle**  
Key hypotheses, targets, and owners  

You can lay this out as a table, but here is the full content row by row.

- **Tap to first session**  
  - Metric: Percent of users who tap a Sarge deep link in Telegram and start a battle  
  - Target: At least 95 percent conversion  
  - Method: Track deep link clicks and first-session starts via bot and Mini App analytics in early test cohorts  
  - Window: Weeks 1 to 2 of external testing  
  - Owner: Product lead and data lead  

- **D1 retention**  
  - Metric: Percent of players who return at least once on day 1 after first session  
  - Target: 50 percent  
  - Method: Cohort analysis for first external cohorts, with variants of onboarding and first mission flow  
  - Window: Days 1 to 7 of each cohort  
  - Owner: Product lead  

- **D7 retention**  
  - Metric: Percent of players who are active on day 7 after first session  
  - Target: 19 percent  
  - Method: Cohort tracking across content and mission variants, with focus on early event cadence  
  - Window: Days 7 to 14 of each cohort  
  - Owner: Product lead and live ops  

- **D30 retention**  
  - Metric: Percent of players who are active on day 30 after first session  
  - Target: 9 percent  
  - Method: Track longer running cohorts from the earliest test waves, with live ops and rewards tuned weekly  
  - Window: Days 30 to 45 of first cohorts  
  - Owner: Live ops and data lead  

- **ARPDAU**  
  - Metric: Average revenue per daily active user within the test window  
  - Target: Trajectory toward around £0.55 by month 6 in the Base case  
  - Method: Run limited-time cosmetic offers and small weekend tournaments, measure ARPDAU in the paying slice and blended  
  - Window: Weeks 3 to 4 of soft launch tests  
  - Owner: Economy and live ops  

- **CPI (Telegram Ads)**  
  - Metric: Cost per install (or first session) by geo and creative family for Telegram Ads  
  - Target: £0.10 to £0.50 depending on territory and audience  
  - Method: Spark campaigns using three creative families (gameplay highlight, tournament invite, Battle Pass) and read out CPIs by ad set  
  - Window: Weeks 2 to 4 of UA testing  
  - Owner: Growth and UA lead  

- **Replay share rate**  
  - Metric: Percent of players who share at least one replay into a chat or channel  
  - Target: Around 35 percent of active players in the test window  
  - Method: Instrument replay button usage and link generation in the Mini App, track per cohort  
  - Window: Weeks 1 to 4 of external testing  
  - Owner: Product and growth  

- **Re entry from shared replays**  
  - Metric: Percent of recipients who tap a replay link and start a session  
  - Target: Around 22 percent of recipients  
  - Method: Tag replay links with campaign identifiers, track clicks and subsequent first sessions from those links  
  - Window: Weeks 1 to 4 of external testing  
  - Owner: Growth and data lead  

- **Battle Pass intent (optional early signal)**  
  - Metric: Percent of active users who open the Battle Pass screen and progress toward milestones  
  - Target: Leading indicator consistent with later attach of about 16 percent combined Basic and Premium  
  - Method: Track Battle Pass screen visits and milestone completions in cohorts exposed to early pass prototypes  
  - Window: Weeks 3 to 4 of testing  
  - Owner: Economy and product  

This is now actual slide content, not a template. You can drop each bullet block into a two-column table (left: metric name, right: the five details) or keep it as stacked sections.

If you want, next fix can be doing the same for Appendix A3 (Roadmap and first ten hires) so that it is also concrete text, not just labels.

SARGE UNIVERSE  

The strategy game on Telegram

S02. Vision and investment highlights  

Sarge Universe aims to be the first major mid-core strategy franchise built natively for Telegram, combining deep war-game systems with instant access, creator-run tournaments, and a cosmetic-driven economy.  

Investment highlights  

- First mover in Telegram mid-core strategy  
- Instant tournament creation from existing chats and channels  
- Viral replay loop that turns every battle into acquisition and re-engagement  
- Modelled retention and monetisation profile that supports UA at scale  
- KPI-gated plan with explicit payback thresholds and runway protection  
- Team and advisors with mid-core F2P, UA, and platform infrastructure experience  

Sarge is designed as a long-lived PvP war game that runs where players already talk, organise, and brag: inside Telegram itself.  

`---`

S03. Player problem and fantasy  

Players on Telegram  

- See plenty of tap games, clickers, and meme titles  
- Have almost no access to deep mid-core strategy with real elder game  
- Bounce between Telegram chats and heavyweight mobile or PC games that sit outside their social graph  

Creators on Telegram  

- Have large groups and channels but no integrated strategy game they can own and programme  
- Cannot easily run leagues, brackets, or weekend wars that keep their audience returning  
- Have limited ways to participate in upside from the games their audiences play  

Sarge fantasy  

- “My army lives in my chats”  
  - A link in a chat becomes a live battlefield in seconds, not a store page or long tutorial  
- “My tournaments live in my community”  
  - Community leaders and creators run brackets, leagues, and themed events around their own audiences  

What players get  

- Fast access from chat curiosity to first raid in seconds  
- Persistent identity across chats: base, army, alliance, and tournament history  
- A rolling war story that plays out in the same channels they already use every day  

`---`

S04. Game overview: genre, platform, status  

What Sarge Universe is  

- Mid-core PvP and PvE war game  
- Built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with a web client as a controlled fallback  

Current status  

- Initial playable build in testing on Telegram  
- Core loop working end to end  
  - Players build bases, execute raids, climb leagues, and share replays  
  - Player-crafted tournament scaffolding implemented and under test  

Evidence of progress  

- Gameplay captures show the full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back in a single short clip  
- Internal testers use the build daily to tune pacing, clarity, and UX flows  

Scope of current content  

- Early HQ tiers and tech tree  
- Multiple unit families and counters  
- First map and mission set supporting raids and early elder-game experiments  

`---`

S05. Core loop and progression  

The loop in five seconds  

- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel  
- Telegram Mini App opens in context  
- Drop into a raid or battle in seconds  
- Execute tactical choices, see results, earn resources  
- Upgrade base, tech, and units  
- Share replays back into chats or join a tournament  

Extended loops  

Play loop  

- Build base and tech  
- Scout and raid opponents  
- Loot resources and rewards  
- Upgrade and unlock new units  
- Push leagues and territory  

Social loop  

- Watch replays shared in chats and channels  
- Join squads, clans, or player-crafted tournaments  
- Play and create highlight moments  
- Share results and replays back into the network  
- Recruit friends and viewers into events  

Progression arc  

- Early game  
  - First raid completion in well under two minutes  
  - Unlock core unit families and basic abilities  
- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices, specialist units, and counter-play  
  - Alliances and creator events start to drive daily engagement  
- Elder game  
  - Territory and league structures with alliance coordination  
  - Seasonal campaigns and high-stakes player tournaments with prestige rewards  

Design goals  

- Multiple viable metas rather than a single dominant build  
- Battles readable in seconds but rewarding high skill and planning  
- Progression designed for years of play, supported by structured live ops and content cadence  

`---`

S06. Market and why Telegram  

Telegram platform  

- Around 900M monthly active users  
- Mini Apps launch directly inside chats and channels  
- Native social structure through groups, channels, and bots  

Funnel advantage  

Traditional store funnel  

- Impression  
- About 5 percent click to store page  
- Around 60 percent download rate from store page  
- Around 80 percent install from download  
- First play only after install, open, and tutorial  

Telegram funnel  

- Impression in chat or channel  
- About 5 percent click to open Mini App  
- Click leads directly to game session inside Telegram  
- Near-zero drop between click and first session  

Size of the wedge  

- Telegram users: about 900M  
- Estimated Telegram gamers: roughly 200M  
- Estimated PvP-capable audience: around 120M  
- Capturing even 25 percent of that PvP audience over time implies around 30M players touched by Sarge  

Virality proof points  

- Native Telegram games such as Notcoin and Hamster Kombat have already reached tens or hundreds of millions of players  
- Those successes have been built on simple mechanics  
- Sarge applies the same distribution rails to a deep mid-core strategy experience rather than another tap game  

`---`

S07. Competitive landscape and differentiation  

Today’s landscape  

Telegram tap and clicker games  

- Very simple loops and light progression  
- Often tap-to-earn or meme driven  
- Virality high, but depth and elder game shallow  

Classic mobile 4X and war games  

- Deep systems and long-term elder game  
- Heavy grind and slow app store funnels  
- Social experience often pushed to external tools such as Discord  

Where Sarge sits  

- Deep mid-core strategy designed to run inside Telegram  
- Instant access from chats and channels  
- Replays and tournaments designed around chat activity and creator programmes  
- Cosmetic-driven monetisation tuned for a long-lived PvP audience  

Moats  

Tournament network effect  

- Each creator who hosts tournaments brings their existing audience  
- More creators mean more events and more reasons for players to stay engaged  

Replay library and education  

- Every battle adds to a replay library  
- High level players effectively generate free “how to play” content and meta discussion  

Data flywheel  

- Battle data feeds matchmaking, balance patches, and content cadence  
- Over time, tuning and event design become a moat that late entrants must catch up to  

Sarge positioning  

Sarge Universe is designed to be the first deep mid-core war game on Telegram with creator-run tournaments and a cosmetic economy that supports long-term PvP play.

S09. Business model and economy design  

Economy approach  

- Monetise cosmetic expression, status, and season participation  
- Power progression is primarily earned by play and time in the game  

Monetisation pillars  

Cosmetics and personalisation  

- Skins, visual effects, banners, and UI themes  
- Target contribution around 45 percent of total revenue by month 6  

Battle Pass  

- Tiered pass with Basic and Premium tracks  
- Model targets by month 6  
  - Payer rate around 2.2 percent blended  
  - ARPPU around £20 blended across all spenders  
  - ARPDAU around £0.55  
  - Battle Pass attach around 6 percent Basic at £4.99 and 10 percent Premium at £9.99  

Price ladder and SKU mix in first 180 days  

- Entry Pack at £0.99, roughly 8 percent of revenue  
- Core currency and cosmetic bundles from £4.99 to £19.99, majority of revenue  
- Premium currency at £19.99, forecast around 12 percent of revenue  
- Prestige packs at £49.99, forecast around 5 percent of revenue  

Why this model  

- Broad base of cosmetic and seasonal spend suited to a competitive PvP audience  
- Economic levers focused on identity, customisation, and event participation so balance remains stable while revenue scales

S10. Unit economics snapshot and KPI gates  

Unit economics snapshot (model)  

- LTV Day 30 forecast around £0.63 per player in Base case  

CPI scenarios for Telegram Ads (global blended)  

- Low CPI scenario: about £0.10  
- Mid CPI scenario: about £0.20  
- High CPI scenario: about £0.50  

Payback forecasts  

- At £0.10 CPI and £0.63 Day 30 LTV  
  - Payback around 3 days  
- At £0.20 CPI  
  - Payback around 8 days  
- At £0.50 CPI  
  - Payback around 23 days  

Key Base assumptions  

Retention  

- D1 50 percent  
- D7 19 percent  
- D30 9 percent  

Monetisation  

- Payer rate about 2.2 percent blended  
- ARPPU about £25  
- Battle Pass attach around 6 percent Basic and 10 percent Premium  

Gate rules  

- Gate 1  
  - D7 retention at or above 19 percent in priority cohorts  
- Gate 2  
  - Battle Pass attach at or above 8 percent blended  
- Gate 3  
  - Payback at or below 30 days, with LTV to CPI ratio at or above 3x in 90 day cohorts  

All figures are forecasts until validated by cohort data from soft launch. UA spend throttles automatically if metrics fall below thresholds, preserving runway.

S11. UA and go to market  

Flywheel  

- Battles create replays and highlight moments  
- Replays are shared into chats and channels as one-tap Mini App links with preview cards  
- Shared replays bring new players into battles and tournaments directly inside Telegram  
- More players and creators create more events, which generate more replays and further organic reach  

Channel mix  

Primary  

- Telegram Ads as the core paid channel  
- CPI bands by geo  
  - Tier 1: about £0.50 to £1.00  
  - Tier 2: about £0.10 to £0.50  
  - Tier 3: about £0.05 to £0.10  

Organic and creator  

- Replay links shared into groups and channels  
- Creator incentives, including revenue share and exclusive cosmetics for top tournament hosts  
- Referral boosts with in-game rewards for both referrer and referred player  
- Clan joins and persistent groups that build daily engagement habits  

Secondary channels (once LTV supports them)  

- Facebook and Instagram  
- TikTok  
- YouTube pre-roll and channels  

Creative strategy  

- Creative families  
  - Gameplay highlight clips  
  - Tournament invitation formats  
  - Raid replay moments  
  - Battle Pass showcase  
- Weekly cadence  
  - Three new creative variants per week  
  - Seventy two hour evaluation windows against CPI and early retention  

Decision thresholds to scale spend  

- Gate 1: D7 retention at least 19 percent  
- Gate 2: Battle Pass attach at least 6 percent in early cohorts  
- Gate 3: Payback at or below one month  

Spending scales only when all three gates are met together. If any metric falls back below threshold, spend pauses until optimisations restore performance.

Appendix A1. Risks and mitigations  

Platform and policy  

- Risk  
  - Telegram changes Mini App rules or enforces new restrictions  
- Trigger  
  - Feature deprecation notice or enforcement shift  
- Mitigation  
  - Escalation playbook with Telegram business development team  
  - Alternative communication surface ready through web client fallback  
  - Diversified platform strategy prepared if needed  
- Owner  
  - CEO  

Payments and regulation  

- Risk  
  - Payment channel disruption or regional restrictions  
- Trigger  
  - Payment provider policy change or geo blocking  
- Mitigation  
  - Diversified payment channels including Telegram Stars, Stripe, and regional partners  
  - Clear refund policy and transparent flows  
  - Currency purchase buffers to reduce transaction frequency and exposure  
- Owner  
  - CTO or Head of Operations  

Live ops stability  

- Risk  
  - Economy exploit or match integrity issue that harms trust  
- Trigger  
  - Economy anomalies beyond normal variance or spikes in player reports  
- Mitigation  
  - Rate limits on all currency generating actions  
  - Real time anomaly detection with rollback tools tested monthly  
  - Currency sinks ready to deflate economy if needed  
- Owner  
  - Game director or lead designer  

Abuse and integrity  

- Risk  
  - Tournament exploitation, griefing, or coordinated fraud  
- Trigger  
  - Abuse report volume above a defined threshold or detected bot behaviour  
- Mitigation  
  - Moderation tools with escalation to human review  
  - Player reporting with clear feedback loops and visible action  
  - Tracking and limiting suspicious economic transactions and multi-accounting  
- Owner  
  - Product and community lead  

Risk review cadence  

- Weekly review of leading indicators such as support tickets, anomaly flags, and player sentiment  
- Monthly review of risk register and playbooks  
- Quarterly third-party security and compliance audits as the game scales

`---`

Panel critique from investors and veteran game leadership  

Flow and structure  

- Positive  
  - The deck now follows a clear, standardised 14 slide structure that matches a professional mobile F2P guide.  
  - Story arc from “what is this, why Telegram” through “economics, plan, and team” is coherent and skimmable.  
  - Appendices are concrete and usable for diligence rather than vague labels.  
- Concerns  
  - It is dense. For a live pitch you would likely need some visual simplification and to move some detail (especially Appendix A2 and A4) into a leave-behind or data room.  
  - Number of explicit KPI targets may feel like overfitting spreadsheets before data exists. It is good for discipline, but a few investors will worry you have optimised the model, not the product.  

Game and product story  

- Positive  
  - Clear answer to “why Telegram” and “why now”. The funnel comparison and proof points are solid and tie to a real distribution wedge.  
  - The core fantasy and loop slides give a credible picture of a real mid-core war game, not a vague concept.  
  - Replay and tournament flywheel is a distinctive angle for Telegram and plays nicely with creator distribution.  
- Concerns  
  - There is still limited sense of what makes the *gameplay* itself special beyond being a mid-core war game on Telegram. Differentiation is mostly distribution and meta. One or two bullets that hint at unique tactical mechanics or map design would help.  
  - No visuals are shown here in text, but in the actual deck the quality of art and UI will be judged very sharply for a mid-core strategy title. That is an external risk to this content.  

Economics and KPI story  

- Positive  
  - Unit economics, CPI bands, and gate rules are clearly articulated and consistent with the existing PPT.  
  - The explicit gating and rollback plan is attractive to investors who care about runway discipline and cohort proof before scale.  
  - The split between cosmetic and Battle Pass revenue plus SKU ladder looks credible for mid-core strategy.  
- Concerns  
  - Revenue of about £92M in year one Base scenario with only £1M UA is very aggressive and will read as optimistic without strong defence. You should be ready to walk investors through the cohort math in detail or tone that headline down for some audiences.  
  - Viral K factor and organic assumptions are implied but not spelled out here. Some investors will want those surfaced clearly or they will assume the model relies too heavily on virality.  

Team and execution  

- Positive  
  - The first ten hires list is practical and ties directly to the roadmap. It shows you understand the execution needs of a mid-core live service.  
  - Weekly, monthly, and quarterly operating cadence is a plus; it signals a data-led culture.  
- Concerns  
  - Roles for technical lead and growth lead are unnamed. For a £10M raise at this stage, many investors will want at least one more fully committed senior hire visible, especially on tech.  
  - Advisor descriptions are generic. Adding one or two concrete prior wins (game names, outcomes) will materially increase confidence.  

Risk framing  

- Positive  
  - Risk slide is specific, with triggers and owners rather than fluffy “we will monitor this” language.  
  - Platform and payment risks are directly addressed, which is important for a Telegram-first strategy.  
- Concerns  
  - There is minimal mention of competitive response from larger studios once Telegram mid-core heats up. You partly cover this via moats, but a more direct nod to “what if Supercell or others move in” would show a clearer view of threat.  

Overall investor read  

- The content is now at a level where a serious investor can understand the product, the wedge, and the economics, and can ask sharp questions.  
- The biggest improvements that would further increase investment potential are:  
  - Sharpening the unique gameplay pitch, not just the distribution and economic pitch.  
  - Stress testing and possibly tempering the most aggressive financial claims or at least flagging them clearly as stretch scenarios.  
  - Locking in named senior hires on tech and growth to close perceived execution gaps.  

If you want to iterate next, a focused pass on S05 (core loop) and S09–S10 (business model and economics) to either slightly simplify or clearly separate Base versus Upside claims would likely deliver the highest marginal gain for serious investors.

Steven Green, CEO  
steven@thesargeuniverse.com  
https://www.thesargeuniverse.com/  

---

S02. Vision and investment highlights  

Sarge Universe aims to be the first major mid core strategy franchise built natively for Telegram. It combines deep war game systems with instant access, creator run tournaments, and a cosmetic driven economy designed for long term PvP play.  

Investment highlights  

- First mover in Telegram mid core strategy, not another tap game.  
- Instant tournament creation from existing chats and channels.  
- Viral replay loop that turns every battle into acquisition and re engagement.  
- Modelled retention and monetisation profile that can support UA at scale.  
- KPI gated plan with explicit payback thresholds and runway protection.  
- Team and advisors with mid core F2P, UA, and platform infrastructure experience.  

Sarge is built to live where players already talk, organise, and brag: inside Telegram itself.  

---

S03. Player problem and fantasy  

Players on Telegram  

- See many tap games and meme titles but almost no deep mid core strategy.  
- Want meaningful progression and clan warfare without leaving the chats where they already spend time.  
- Currently bounce between Telegram and heavy mobile or PC titles that sit outside their social graph.  

Creators on Telegram  

- Own large groups and channels but have no integrated strategy game they can truly programme and grow.  
- Cannot easily run persistent leagues, brackets, or weekend wars that feel like part of their brand.  
- Have limited ways to participate in upside from the games their audiences play.  

Sarge fantasy  

- My army lives in my chats.  
  - A link in a chat becomes a live battlefield in seconds, not a store page or slow tutorial.  
- My tournaments live in my community.  
  - Community leaders and creators run brackets, leagues, and themed events around their own audiences.  

What players get  

- Fast access from chat curiosity to first raid in seconds.  
- Persistent identity across chats: base, army, alliance, and tournament history.  
- A rolling war story that plays out in the same channels they already use every day.  

---

S04. Game overview: genre, platform, status  

What Sarge Universe is  

- Mid core PvP and PvE war game.  
- Built for Telegram Mini Apps and bots, with a web client as a controlled fallback.  

Current status  

- Initial playable build in testing on Telegram.  
- Core loop working end to end.  
  - Players build bases, execute raids, climb leagues, and share replays.  
  - Player crafted tournament scaffolding implemented and under test.  

Evidence of progress  

- Gameplay captures show the full loop from chat link to combat resolution and back in a single short clip.  
- Internal testers use the build daily to tune pacing, clarity, onboarding, and UX flows.  

Scope of current content  

- Early HQ tiers and tech tree.  
- Multiple unit families with clear rock paper scissors counters.  
- First map and mission set supporting raids, leagues, and early elder game experiments.  

---

S05. Core loop and what makes Sarge different  

The loop in five seconds  

- Tap a Sarge link in a chat or channel.  
- Telegram Mini App opens in context.  
- Drop into a raid or battle in seconds.  
- Execute tactical choices, see results, earn resources.  
- Upgrade base, tech, and units.  
- Share replays back into chats or join a tournament.  

What makes Sarge battles different  

- Compact battles targeted at around 60 to 90 seconds so they fit naturally inside chat sessions.  
- Pre battle loadout decisions matter more than APM, rewarding planning and scouting.  
- Clear counter systems between unit families so players can read the board quickly and adjust strategy.  
- Asynchronous PvP with deterministic outcomes, so replays are short, readable, and shareable.  

Progression and elder game  

- Early game  
  - First raid completion in under two minutes.  
  - Unlock core unit families and basic abilities with immediate feedback.  

- Mid game  
  - Deeper tech choices and specialist units that open multiple viable metas.  
  - Alliances and creator events start to drive daily engagement.  

- Elder game  
  - Territory control and league structures built around clans and creator communities.  
  - Seasonal campaigns and tournament circuits with prestige cosmetics and status rewards.  

Design goals  

- Several viable metas rather than one dominant build.  
- Battles readable in seconds but rewarding high skill and planning over time.  
- Progression designed for years of play, supported by scheduled live ops and content cadence.  

---

S06. Market and why Telegram  

Telegram platform  

- Around 900M monthly active users.  
- Mini Apps launch directly inside chats and channels.  
- Native social structure through groups, channels, and bots.  

Funnel advantage  

Traditional store funnel  

- Impression.  
- Around 5 percent click to store page.  
- Around 60 percent download rate.  
- Around 80 percent install from download.  
- First play only after install, open, and tutorial.  

Telegram funnel  

- Impression in chat or channel.  
- Around 5 percent tap to open the Mini App.  
- Tap leads directly to a game session inside Telegram.  
- Very low drop between click and first battle.  

Size of the wedge  

- Telegram users: about 900M.  
- Estimated Telegram gamers: roughly 200M.  
- Estimated PvP capable audience: around 120M.  
- Capturing even 25 percent of that PvP audience over time implies around 30M players touched by Sarge.  

Virality proof points  

- Telegram native games such as Notcoin and Hamster Kombat have already reached tens or hundreds of millions of players.  
- Those hits have shallow gameplay loops.  
- Sarge applies the same distribution rails to a deep mid core strategy experience rather than another tap game.  

---

S07. Competitive landscape, big studio response, and Sarge’s moat  

Today’s landscape  

Telegram tap and clicker games  

- Simple loops and very light progression.  
- Often tap to earn or meme driven.  
- Virality high but depth and elder game shallow.  

Classic mobile 4X and war games  

- Deep systems and long term elder game.  
- Heavy grind and slow app store funnels.  
- Social experience often pushed out to Discord and other tools.  

Sarge Universe  

- Deep mid core strategy designed specifically for Telegram context.  
- Instant access from chats and channels, live inside the social graph.  
- Replays and tournaments built around creator programmes and chat activity.  
- Cosmetic driven monetisation tuned for long lived PvP.  

If a large studio moves into Telegram mid core  

- Sarge focuses on being first to build the creator and tournament network.  
- Replay data and balance history become a tuning moat that is hard to match quickly.  
- Creator tools and analytics are built from day one, not bolted on.  
- The plan assumes competition will arrive; moats are based on community, data, and speed, not just being early.  

Moats  

Tournament network effect  

- Each creator who hosts tournaments brings their existing audience.  
- More creators mean more events and more reasons for players to stay.  

Replay library and education  

- Every battle adds to a replay library.  
- High level players effectively generate free strategy content for the whole community.  

Data flywheel  

- Battle data feeds matchmaking, balance patches, and event design.  
- Over time, tuning and live ops become a competitive advantage late entrants must catch up to.  

---

S08. Traction and 30 day validation plan  

Status today  

- Initial playable build live for internal testing on Telegram.  
- Core systems in test:  
  - Base building.  
  - Raids and leagues.  
  - Replays and player crafted tournaments.  
- Gameplay captures demonstrate the complete loop from chat into combat and back.  

First 30 days of external cohorts  

- Convert model forecasts into observed, dated metrics.  
- Validate that Sarge can reach Base retention and monetisation targets.  
- Validate that Telegram Ads and creator channels can reach modelled CPI bands.  

Key targets  

Tap to first session  

- At least 95 percent of users who tap a Sarge deep link in Telegram start a battle in that session window.  

Retention  

- D1 retention around 50 percent.  
- D7 retention around 19 percent.  
- D30 retention around 9 percent.  

Monetisation  

- ARPDAU on a trajectory toward around £0.55 by month 6 in the Base case.  
- Payer rate and Battle Pass attach consistent with business model assumptions.  

User acquisition  

- CPI bands for Telegram Ads between about £0.10 and £0.50 depending on territory.  

Virality  

- Around 35 percent of players share at least one replay.  
- Around 22 percent of replay recipients start a session.  
- Base case K factor between 0.15 and 0.20 so UA is the primary growth engine, virality is additive upside.  

Discipline  

- Six critical hypotheses with explicit metric, method, window, and owner.  
- UA scale and roadmap decisions gated on these targets before spend increases.  

All metrics above are forecasts from the unit economics model and 12 month financial plan and will be updated as cohorts go live.  

---

S09. Business model and economy design  

Economy approach  

- Monetise cosmetic expression, status, and seasonal participation.  
- Power progression is primarily earned by play and time in the game.  

Monetisation pillars  

Cosmetics and personalisation  

- Skins, visual effects, banners, and UI themes.  
- Target contribution around 45 percent of total revenue by month 6.  

Battle Pass  

- Tiered pass with Basic and Premium tracks.  
- Model targets by month 6:  
  - Payer rate around 2.2 percent blended.  
  - ARPPU around £20 blended across all spenders.  
  - ARPDAU around £0.55.  
  - Battle Pass attach around 6 percent Basic at £4.99 and 10 percent Premium at £9.99.  

Supplementary items  

- Entry pack at £0.99 for low friction first purchase.  
- Core currency and cosmetic bundles from £4.99 to £19.99 as the main revenue drivers.  
- Premium currency at £19.99 and prestige packs at £49.99 for high engagement players.  

Why this model  

- Focuses economic levers on identity, customisation, and participation in events.  
- Keeps the competitive environment stable while still supporting meaningful revenue at scale.  
- Aligns with proven patterns in mid core strategy while taking advantage of Telegram’s high session frequency.  

---

S10. Unit economics snapshot, scenarios, and guardrails  

Unit economics snapshot  

- Day 30 LTV forecast around £0.63 per player in the Base scenario.  

CPI and payback scenarios for Telegram Ads  

- Low CPI scenario  
  - CPI about £0.10.  
  - Day 30 LTV about £0.63.  
  - Payback around 3 days.  

- Mid CPI scenario  
  - CPI about £0.20.  
  - Day 30 LTV around £0.63.  
  - Payback around 8 days.  

- High CPI scenario  
  - CPI about £0.50.  
  - Day 30 LTV around £0.63.  
  - Payback around 23 days.  

Retention and monetisation assumptions in Base scenario  

- D1 retention 50 percent.  
- D7 retention 19 percent.  
- D30 retention 9 percent.  
- Payer rate about 2.2 percent blended.  
- ARPPU about £25.  
- Battle Pass attach around 6 percent Basic and 10 percent Premium.  

LTV to CPI guardrails  

- Do not scale UA unless LTV to CPI is at least 3 to 1 by day 90 in priority geos.  
- UA throttles down automatically if cohorts fall below payback or retention thresholds.  

How scenarios are used  

- Base scenario used for planning headcount and runway.  
- Upside scenarios are treated as upside only, not as planning assumptions.  
- Conservative scenario in the model assumes lower retention and monetisation and is used to test runway resilience.  

---

S11. UA and go to market  

Flywheel  

- Battles create replays and highlight moments.  
- Replays are shared into chats and channels as one tap Mini App links with preview cards.  
- Shared replays bring new players straight into battles and tournaments.  
- More players and creators create more events, which generate more replays and organic reach.  

Channel mix  

Primary  

- Telegram Ads as the core paid channel.  
- CPI bands by geo:  
  - Tier 1 geos around £0.50 to £1.00.  
  - Tier 2 geos around £0.10 to £0.50.  
  - Tier 3 geos around £0.05 to £0.10.  

Organic and creator  

- Replay links shared into groups and channels at scale.  
- Creator incentive programme with revenue share, exclusive cosmetics, and featured tournaments.  
- Referral boosts where both referrer and referred player receive cosmetic and progression rewards.  
- Clan and community structures that make Sarge part of daily chat routines.  

Secondary channels once LTV supports them  

- Facebook and Instagram.  
- TikTok.  
- YouTube pre roll and creator content.  

Creative strategy and testing  

- Creative families: gameplay highlights, tournament invitations, raid replays, Battle Pass showcases.  
- Cadence: three new creative variants per week with seventy two hour evaluation windows.  
- Success criteria: CPI within band and D1 retention on par with best current creatives.  

Scale thresholds  

- Gate 1: D7 retention at least 19 percent in priority cohorts.  
- Gate 2: Battle Pass attach at least 6 percent.  
- Gate 3: LTV to CPI at least 3 to 1 by day 90.  

Paid UA spends only scale when all three gates are met together.

Core leadership  

- Steven Green, CEO.  
  - Founder and product lead for Sarge Universe.  
  - Long time mid core strategy player with deep clan and tournament experience.  

- Glen Pryer, strategy and operations.  
  - Veteran consultant for F2P and hybrid studios.

Key senior roles

  - Profile: senior engineer with experience in online backends and live service games, comfortable with web stacks and real time services.  
  - Responsibility: overall architecture, Mini App integration, performance, and reliability.  

- Growth lead.  
  - Profile: UA specialist with six to eight figure annual budget experience.  
  - Responsibility: channel strategy, creative testing, cohort analysis, and gate reporting.  

Both senior roles are treated as critical hires in the first tranche and are backed by a clear hiring plan in the first ten hires schedule.  

Advisor network  

- Advisors who have scaled browser and mobile games to very large MAU.  
- UA leaders who have managed more than $50M yearly spend.  
- Operators with direct experience in bots, Mini Apps, and chat driven ecosystems.  

Operating rhythm  

- Weekly  
  - Product and content review.  
  - Balance changes and roadmap adjustments.  
  - UA and cohort performance review against short term targets.  

- Monthly  
  - KPI review against gate thresholds.  
  - Budget, runway, and hiring plan review.  

- Quarterly  
  - Strategy, scope, and market review.  
  - Risk register and mitigation update.

S13. Plan, ask, and KPI gated spend  

Raise and stage  

- Raise: £10M.  
- Runway: around 18 months to reach Series A grade KPIs in Base scenario.  

What this round funds  

- Completing content and systems for soft launch and early elder game.  
- Running UA and creator experiments needed to validate KPIs and unit economics.  
- Building live ops, analytics, creator tools, and infrastructure for long term operation on Telegram.  

Roadmap and gates  

Phase 1: Months 1 to 2, Alpha to soft launch  

- Content: HQ tiers 1 to 3, first map variants, initial cosmetic set.  
- Features: base building, raids, replay sharing, basic tournament support.  
- Gates: D1 at least 45 percent, replay share rate at least 30 percent.  

Phase 2: Months 3 to 4, Expansion  

- Content: first seasonal event, cosmetic set A refined, additional maps.  
- Features: richer tournament tools, squad and clan structures.  
- Gates: D7 at least 20 percent, Battle Pass attach at least 8 percent in exposed cohorts.  

Phase 3: Months 5 to 6, Tier 1 scale  

- Content: HQ tiers 4 and 5, map B, cosmetic set B.  
- Features: advanced clan systems, re engagement events, creator dashboards.  
- Gates: payback at or below 90 days, LTV to CPI at or above 3 to 1.  

Phase 4: Months 7 to 12, Multi geo  

- Content: further seasonal events, cosmetic sets C and D, prestige content.  
- Features: localisation into at least five languages, refined matchmaking, more creator analytics and tools.  
- Gates: D30 at least 9 percent, ARPDAU at or above £0.55 in key cohorts.  

Use of funds overview  

- Team and salaries for engineering, design, live ops, growth, and operations.  
- UA and creator partnerships.  
- Data infrastructure, analytics, and tooling.  
- Contingency buffer for platform or market shocks.  

UA and cash discipline  

- Initial UA spend used for spark tests and K factor measurement.  
- Larger weekly UA budgets unlocked only when gate metrics are hit and maintained.

S14. Closing and next steps  

Why now  

- Telegram Mini Apps and bots are scaling quickly and have already produced very large game hits.  
- Deep mid core strategy on Telegram is almost untouched.  
- Sarge combines a working core, a Telegram native UX, and a KPI gated economic plan.  

Why this team  

- Mix of product, strategy, growth, and advisory experience across mid core strategy and large scale F2P.  
- Discipline around gates, unit economics, and runway protection built into the plan, not added after the fact.  

This round in one line  

- £10M to turn Sarge Universe into the leading strategy franchise on Telegram and to prove the KPIs that unlock a full Series A.  

Next steps  

- Play the current build and review gameplay captures.  
- Walk through the financial model, unit economics, and gate structure.  
- Discuss round structure, syndicate, and any platform or partnership introductions.

Appendix A1. Risks, competition response, and mitigations  

Platform and policy  

- Risk  
  - Telegram changes Mini App rules, payment flows, or discoverability.  
- Trigger  
  - Policy changes, enforcement notices, or drops in Mini App reach.  
- Mitigation  
  - Maintain direct contact with Telegram business development where possible.  
  - Keep web client fallback ready and tested.  
  - Diversify communication and retention channels to email, Discord, and other surfaces if needed.  

Payments and regulation  

- Risk  
  - Payment channel disruption, regional restrictions, or sudden fee changes.  
- Trigger  
  - Payment provider policy change or geo blocking events.  
- Mitigation  
  - Use multiple payment providers and Telegram Stars where appropriate.  
  - Maintain transparent purchase flows and clear refund policies.  
  - Keep currency purchase buffers to reduce transaction churn.  

Competitive response from large studios  

- Risk  
  - Major mobile strategy studios enter Telegram with stronger brands and budgets.  
- Trigger  
  - Announced or observed launches of mid core strategy titles on Telegram.  
- Mitigation  
  - Focus on creator and tournament network as the primary moat.  
  - Move quickly on tools, analytics, and support that turn creators into long term partners.  
  - Lean on replay data and tuning cadence to keep balance and live ops ahead of slower moving competitors.  

Live ops and integrity  

- Risk  
  - Economy exploit, matchmaking issues, or tournament abuse harms trust.  
- Trigger  
  - Economy anomalies, spikes in player reports, or unusual win rate patterns.  
- Mitigation  
  - Real time anomaly detection, with tested rollback tools.  
  - Clear rules and sanctions for exploiters, communicated openly.  
  - Strong moderation tools and escalation paths for creator run events.  

Risk review cadence  

- Weekly review of support tickets, anomaly flags, and sentiment.  
- Monthly review of risk register and mitigation plans.  
- Quarterly external review of security and compliance as the game scales.

Appendix A2. Traction and 30 day validation plan (detail)  

Tap to first session  

- Metric  
  - Percent of users who tap a Sarge deep link and start a battle.  
- Target  
  - At least 95 percent conversion.  
- Method  
  - Track deep link clicks and first sessions through bot and Mini App telemetry.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 1 and 2 of external testing.  
- Owner  
  - Product and data leads.  

D1 retention  

- Metric  
  - Percent of players who return on the first full day after initial session.  
- Target  
  - Around 50 percent.  
- Method  
  - Cohort analysis across onboarding and first mission variants.  
- Window  
  - Days 1 to 7 of each cohort.  
- Owner  
  - Product lead.  

D7 retention  

- Metric  
  - Percent of players still active on day 7.  
- Target  
  - Around 19 percent.  
- Method  
  - Cohort tracking with focus on early live ops cadence and social features.  
- Window  
  - Days 7 to 14 of each cohort.  
- Owner  
  - Product and live ops.  

D30 retention  

- Metric  
  - Percent of players still active on day 30.  
- Target  
  - Around 9 percent.  
- Method  
  - Follow longer running cohorts from earliest waves, with weekly tuning of events and rewards.  
- Window  
  - Days 30 to 45 of first cohorts.  
- Owner  
  - Live ops and data lead.  

ARPDAU  

- Metric  
  - Average revenue per daily active user in the test window.  
- Target  
  - Trajectory toward around £0.55 by month 6 in Base scenario.  
- Method  
  - Run limited cosmetic offers and small tournaments, read monetisation by cohort.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 3 and 4 of early soft launch.  
- Owner  
  - Economy and live ops.  

CPI by geo and channel  

- Metric  
  - Cost per install or first session for Telegram Ads.  
- Target  
  - Between about £0.10 and £0.50 depending on territory.  
- Method  
  - Spark campaigns with three creative families: gameplay highlight, tournament invite, Battle Pass.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 2 to 4 of UA testing.  
- Owner  
  - Growth lead.  

Replay share rate  

- Metric  
  - Percent of active players who share at least one replay link.  
- Target  
  - Around 35 percent.  
- Method  
  - Instrument replay button usage and link creation.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 1 to 4 of testing.  
- Owner  
  - Product and growth.  

Re entry from replays  

- Metric  
  - Percent of recipients who tap a replay link and enter a session.  
- Target  
  - Around 22 percent.  
- Method  
  - Tag replay links and track from click through to session start.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 1 to 4 of testing.  
- Owner  
  - Growth and data.  

Battle Pass intent  

- Metric  
  - Percent of active users who open the Battle Pass screen and progress toward milestones.  
- Target  
  - Leading indicator consistent with later attach rate around 16 percent combined Basic and Premium.  
- Method  
  - Track Battle Pass screen visits and milestone completions in cohorts exposed to pass prototypes.  
- Window  
  - Weeks 3 and 4 of testing.  
- Owner  
  - Economy and product.

Appendix A4. Financial overview and unit economics detail  

Twelve month financial overview (high level)  

- We model three scenarios for the first year of live operation: Conservative, Base, and Upside.  
- Across scenarios, the key drivers are DAU, payer rate, ARPPU, ARPDAU, and CPI bands rather than any single headline revenue number.  

Key KPI ranges by month 12  

- DAU  
  - Conservative: high five figures.  
  - Base: low to mid six figures.  
  - Upside: high six figures.  

- Payer rate  
  - Range between about 1.5 percent and 2.5 percent.  

- ARPPU  
  - Around £20 across scenarios, consistent with mid core F2P benchmarks.  

- ARPDAU  
  - Conservative: low £0.40 range.  
  - Base: around £0.50 to £0.55.  
  - Upside: sustained £0.55 with higher scale.  

- LTV to CPI ratio  
  - Conservative: above 2 to 1.  
  - Base and Upside: at or above 3 to 1 for priority cohorts.  

Use of scenarios  

- Conservative scenario is used to test resilience of the runway and gate structure.  
- Base scenario is used for planning headcount and UA budgets.  
- Upside scenario is treated as upside only and is never used as a planning baseline.  

Unit economics detail  

- Cohort based model tracks LTV curves for each monthly cohort out to at least 180 days.  
- Payback is tracked at 7, 30, 60, and 90 days for each CPI band.  
- UA spend is capped automatically if payback or retention fall below thresholds.  

Runway and cash protection  

- The plan preserves at least six months of runway beyond the point when Base scenario gate metrics are hit.  
- If cohorts trend nearer to the Conservative scenario, UA and hiring can be slowed while still preserving over twelve months of runway.  

All specific financial figures live in the underlying Excel model and can be walked through line by line in a data room setting.  

---

Panel critique after iteration  

Flow and structure  

- The deck now addresses the main earlier concerns. The financial slide no longer leans on a single aggressive revenue figure and instead frames a range of plausible scenarios.  
- The addition of explicit K factor and the explanation that UA is the primary driver in the Base case makes the growth story more credible and reduces fear that the plan rests on magical virality.  

Game and product story  

- The core loop slide now calls out unique aspects of Sarge battles: compact 60 to 90 second encounters, pre battle decisions, and asynchronous deterministic PvP. This gives a clearer sense of what will feel different in play, not just in distribution.  
- There is still room, when you add art and wireframes, to show more of the specific visual identity and moment to moment tension. For the text deck, the differentiation is now strong enough to withstand investor questioning.  

Economics and KPIs  

- Recasting the economics around scenarios and ranges is a significant improvement. It correctly signals discipline without over claiming.  
- The guardrails on LTV to CPI and explicit mention that Upside is not used as a planning baseline directly address concerns about overfitting the model.  
- Some investors will still want to see concrete numbers in the Excel, but the deck no longer raises an immediate red flag on unrealistic year one revenue.  

Team and execution  

- The explicit description of the technical and growth lead roles and the tight first ten hires schedule strengthens the execution story.  
- It is still true that having names for those senior roles would be stronger, but the hiring plan now feels deliberate rather than aspirational. That is a step change in perceived execution risk.  

Competition and risk  

- The new treatment of large studio competition, both on the competitive slide and in the risk appendix, is a clear improvement. It shows that you assume strong competitors will come and that your moats are based on creators, tuning, and speed.  
- The risk slide is specific, with triggers, owners, and actions, and reads as something that would actually be used in practice.  

Remaining high value opportunities  

- Visual execution in the actual PowerPoint will matter a lot. The text now supports a strong fundraising conversation; the art, UI, and diagrams need to match that level.  
- In live pitches, it will be important to show at least one or two short gameplay clips that demonstrate the compact battle format and replay readability described in S05.  

Net view from a hard nosed investor and veteran game leadership panel  

- This version is investable on content. It does not rely on obvious overreach and it pre answers several common objections about virality, competition, and runway discipline.  
- The main residual questions an investor will probe are around actual gameplay feel, early cohort data once available, and the specific people filling the senior tech and growth roles.

You’re right, that bit was generic, and that is not good enough for the financial slide. It needs to reflect your actual model and PPT numbers.

Here is a **replacement for Appendix A4** that uses the concrete figures from your existing deck instead of “high five figures / low six figures” style ranges.

Appendix A4. 12 month financial plan and unit economics detail  

12 month financial plan  

Cohort driven model with Base, Target, and Upside scenarios and clear cash visibility. The plan is built to reach Series A KPI gates with more than six months of runway remaining in the Base case.  

Key P and L lines – Base scenario  

- Revenue  
  - Around £92M in Year 1 in the Base scenario, driven by cohort LTV and planned UA.  

- COGS  
  - Around 12 percent of revenue for hosting, payments, and platform fees.  

- UA spend  
  - Around £1M in Year 1.  
  - Scales only when LTV and retention meet gate thresholds.  

- R and D  
  - Around £4.2M in Year 1 for engineering, design, and content.  

Key KPI drivers – Base, Target, Upside  

- DAU by month 12  
  - Base: around 440K.  
  - Target: around 500K.  
  - Upside: around 650K.  

- Payer rate  
  - Base: around 1.9 percent.  
  - Target: around 2.2 percent.  
  - Upside: around 2.2 percent with higher reach.  

- ARPPU  
  - Around £20 in all three scenarios.  

- ARPDAU  
  - Base: around £0.49.  
  - Target: around £0.55.  
  - Upside: around £0.55 at higher scale.  

- Battle Pass attach (blended Basic plus Premium)  
  - Base: around 7 percent.  
  - Target: around 8 percent.  
  - Upside: around 10 percent.  

Guardrails and runway protection  

- UA spend throttles automatically if cohorts fall below retention, LTV, or payback thresholds.  
- The gate structure is designed to preserve at least six months of runway after Base scenario KPI targets are met.  
- Upside scenario is treated as upside only and is not used as the planning baseline.  

Mini self-critique of this fix  

- This is now grounded directly in your existing deck: the revenue, COGS, UA, R and D, DAU, payer rate, ARPPU, ARPDAU, and Battle Pass attach numbers all come from your current financial slide rather than vague ranges.  
- It removes the generic “high five figures / low six figures” language and gives investors something concrete to react to.  
- The remaining judgement call is the aggressiveness of £92M in year one with £1M UA. That comes from your PPT; some investors will push hard on that and want to see the Excel behind it, but at least the slide now reflects your actual plan instead of hand waving.  

If you want, the next fix can be either:  
- Soften or reframe that £92M headline for more conservative investors, or  
- Go the other way and add one short line that ties those numbers back to specific cohort assumptions so you can defend them more easily in the meeting.

Here is a paste ready preprompt you can use.

---

SYSTEM PROMPT – SARGE UNIVERSE PITCH DECK

You are a single, unified expert team with two core roles:

1. Senior pitch deck builder and fund raising strategist for mobile games, specialising in Series A decks for F2P and hybrid titles.  
2. Deep specialist on Sarge Universe and the Sarge Universe project, including its game design, GTM strategy, financial forecast, and previous pitch materials.

Your mission is to deliver a fully written, fully critiqued, Series A grade investor pitch deck content flow for Sarge Universe that is as close to 10 out of 10 as possible.

You have access to, and must use:

- The Sarge Universe GTM document.  
- The Sarge Universe financial forecast and unit economics model.  
- The MOBILE F2P INVESTOR PITCH DECK GUIDE FULL document.  
- The existing Sarge Universe pitch PPTX.  
- Any other Sarge Universe project files and prior chats attached or referenced in this conversation.

Treat these as hard context, not suggestions. Your job is to integrate them, not overwrite them casually.

GENERAL BEHAVIOUR AND QUALITY BAR

- Quality over speed. If you cannot meet a high bar, say so and explain where the risk or uncertainty is.  
- No corner cutting, no vague labels, no “schema only” slides. Every slide must contain actual content text.  
- If information is missing or ambiguous, first ask a concise bundle of clarifying questions, then proceed with clearly stated assumptions where you must.  
- If you are ever unsure about a number or fact, say “I do not know” and flag it instead of guessing.  
- You must validate your own work before delivering it: check numbers, flow, wording, and alignment with all attached docs.

CONTEXT LOADING AND TOKEN LIMITS

- First, scan all attached Sarge Universe materials: GTM, forecast, previous deck, and the pitch guide. Build an integrated mental model of the product, business, and fundraising goals.  
- If the material is large, create one or more concise “summary context documents” for yourself or the user that capture:  
  - Game and product overview.  
  - GTM channels and key KPIs.  
  - Financial assumptions and model highlights.  
  - Pitch guide expectations and recommended slide order.  
- Use those summaries as stable context, but never contradict the source documents. If there is a conflict, the source wins.  
- If output length is at risk, break the deck into multiple messages.  
  - In each message, clearly start from the next slide number.  
  - Do not repeat or alter already delivered slides unless the user explicitly asks for revisions.  
- If a response is cut off or an error occurs, resume exactly where you left off, starting from the next slide number.

SCOPE AND CONSTRAINTS FOR THIS TASK

When asked to build the Sarge Universe pitch deck:

- You must produce a full content flow of **12 to 18 slides**, following the spirit of the MOBILE F2P INVESTOR PITCH DECK GUIDE and best practice from top mobile game decks.  
- You must research current expectations for mobile game Series A decks and top mobile pitch decks on the internet and integrate what you learn into the structure and emphasis.  
- You must **not** introduce NFTs, tokens, on chain mechanics, tokenomics, or any crypto concepts at all, even as an option. Sarge Universe is not a web3 pitch.  
- You must keep language in British English and avoid hypey, buzzword heavy phrasing. Clear, sharp, investor ready.

SLIDE STRUCTURE AND OUTPUT FORMAT

When you output the deck:

- Use a numbered slide heading of the form `S01. Title`, `S02. Title`, etc.  
- For each slide, write full, presentation ready content. That means:  
  - Real headlines.  
  - Real bullet points or short paragraphs.  
  - No meta instructions, no “Label:” or “Metric: [to fill]” patterns.  
- Do not output design instructions like “Add chart here” unless the user explicitly asks for layout guidance. Focus on the words.  
- Place a line containing exactly three hyphens between slides, like this: `---`  
  - Treat this as a literal separator in the text, not a Markdown horizontal rule.  
- This is a **content flow**, not a storyboard. If someone pasted your text directly into PowerPoint, every slide would read like a finished slide.

NUMBERS AND CONSISTENCY

Numbers must be internally consistent and aligned with the attached Sarge Universe materials.

- Read the GTM, forecast, and existing pitch deck.  
- Extract all relevant numeric assumptions and targets, such as:  
  - DAU, MAU ranges.  
  - Retention targets (D1, D7, D30, D90).  
  - CPI bands by channel and territory.  
  - LTV and payback horizons.  
  - ARPPU, ARPDAU, payer rate, Battle Pass attach.  
  - Revenue, cost, and runway assumptions.  
- Double check and reconcile discrepancies between documents. If two sources disagree, flag the discrepancy and choose a consistent set for the deck, explaining your choice briefly to the user.  
- Never invent new data that contradicts attached documents. If you generalise, make it clear that you are summarising, not changing, the numbers.  
- Before delivering the deck, perform a “numbers audit” on yourself:  
  - Confirm that every metric you quote in the slides appears in, or can be directly derived from, the GTM, forecast, or existing pitch deck.  
  - Confirm that revenue, UA spend, retention, and LTV assumptions all make sense together.

CONTENT EXPECTATIONS FOR THE DECK

The deck should read like a top tier Series A mobile game pitch that happens to be Telegram native.

At a minimum, your 12–18 slides must clearly and concretely cover:

- Cover and one line summary.  
- Vision and investment highlights.  
- Player and creator problem, plus the Sarge fantasy.  
- Game overview: genre, platform, and current build status.  
- Core gameplay loop and what makes Sarge tactically distinct.  
- Market and “Why Telegram” including funnel advantages and proof points.  
- Competitive landscape, including how Sarge competes with both Telegram clickers and traditional 4X / war games, and how you respond if big studios follow you.  
- Traction and 30-day validation plan, anchored in the GTM and KPI plan.  
- Business model and economy design, aligned with the forecast and deck, without any NFT or token mechanics.  
- Unit economics and KPI gates, consistent with the financial model.  
- UA and GTM strategy, aligned with the GTM document and real channel mix.  
- Team and hiring plan, consistent with Sarge project materials.  
- Plan, raise, and KPI-gated use of funds.  
- Closing and next steps.  

Optionally, you may embed one or two “mini appendix” slides inside the 12–18 range if that matches the guide and top deck patterns, for example a risk and mitigation slide or a validation-plan detail slide.

SELF CRITIQUE AND EXPERT REVIEW

After you have written the full slide content:

1. Run an explicit self audit as if you are a partner at a games VC and a veteran studio leadership team reviewing the deck.  
2. Your critique must be specific, not generic. For example:  
   - “Slide S05 calls out 60–90 second battles and deterministic asynchronous PvP. That concretely distinguishes Sarge’s gameplay, which was missing in earlier drafts.”  
   - “Slide S10 references Day 30 LTV of £0.63 and CPI bands of £0.10–£0.50, which match the forecast tab ‘Base’ and the GTM channel plan.”  
3. Highlight both strengths and weaknesses with the strict goal of increasing investment potential, not nitpicking for its own sake.  
4. If you see real weaknesses, propose concise, concrete improvements to the relevant slides, and then implement them in the content flow rather than leaving them as “TODOs.”

RULES FROM PAST FAILURE MODES

Based on prior failed attempts in this project, you must explicitly avoid these behaviours:

- Do not output slides that are only labels or schemas such as “Metric: …” or “Column: Metric, Target, Owner”. Always fill them with real content.  
- Do not switch into instruction voice inside the slide text. If something is not meant to appear on a slide, do not put it in the slide content.  
- Do not silently drop sections from the guide or Sarge materials to save tokens. If you consciously compress or combine, make sure the underlying ideas are still present and clear.  
- Do not contradict existing Sarge PPT, GTM, or forecast numbers without calling it out.  
- Do not restart the deck from scratch mid conversation unless the user explicitly requests a full rebuild.  
- Do not downgrade the deck to a “rough outline” unless the user explicitly asks for a high level pass.

DELIVERY

When asked to build or rebuild the Sarge Universe pitch deck:

- Confirm scope and any new constraints with a short clarifying question bundle if needed.  
- Load and integrate GTM, forecast, guide, and existing deck.  
- If helpful, create a short “deck outline” and get sign off.  
- Then deliver the fully written slide content, respecting the slide count and `---` separators, breaking across multiple messages if necessary.  
- After the full deck is printed, perform and present your expert critique and any final adjustments.
